      <p><b>Russia</b> (Russian: <span lang="ru">Ð Ð¾ÑÑÐ¸Ñ</span>, <i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian-language text">Rossiya</i>, <small>Russian pronunciation:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian" title="Help:IPA/Russian">[rÉËsÊ²ijÉ]</a></span>), or the <b>Russian Federation</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[c]</a></sup> is a country spanning <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Asia" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Asia">Northern Asia</a>. It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">largest country in the world</a>, covering over 17&nbsp;million square kilometres (6.6<span style="margin-left:0.2em">Ã<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>6</sup>&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), and encompassing more than one-eighth of <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>'s inhabited land area. Russia extends across <a href="/wiki/Time_in_Russia" title="Time in Russia">eleven time zones</a>, and has borders with <a href="/wiki/Borders_of_Russia" title="Borders of Russia">sixteen sovereign nations</a>. It has a population of 146.2 million; and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_countries_by_population" title="List of European countries by population">most populous country</a> in Europe, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">ninth-most populous country</a> in the world. <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, the capital, is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_cities_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="List of European cities by population">largest city in Europe</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a> is the nation's <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Russia_by_population" title="List of cities and towns in Russia by population">second-largest city</a> and cultural centre. <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> are the largest <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">European nation</a>; they speak <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>, the most spoken <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">Slavic language</a>, and the most spoken <a href="/wiki/Native_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Native language">native language</a> in Europe. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/East_Slavs" title="East Slavs">East Slavs</a> emerged as a recognisable group in Europe between the 3rd and 8th centuries AD. The <a href="/wiki/Medieval" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval">medieval</a> state of <a href="/wiki/Rus_(state)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rus (state)">Rus'</a> arose in the 9th century. In 988, it adopted <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christianity</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a>, beginning the synthesis of Byzantine and Slavic cultures that defined <a href="/wiki/Russian_culture" title="Russian culture">Russian culture</a> for the next millennium. Rus' ultimately disintegrated until it was finally reunified by the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Moscow" title="Grand Duchy of Moscow">Grand Duchy of Moscow</a> in the 15th century. By the 18th century, the nation had greatly expanded through conquest, annexation, and <a href="/wiki/Russian_explorers" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian explorers">exploration</a> to become the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_empires" title="List of largest empires">third-largest empire</a> in history. Following the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian SFSR</a> became the largest and leading <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">constituent</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, the world's first constitutionally <a href="/wiki/Socialist_state" title="Socialist state">socialist state</a>. The Soviet Union played a <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">decisive role</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> victory in <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, and emerged as a <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpower</a> and rival to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. The Soviet era saw some of the <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Russian_inventions_and_technology_records" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of Russian inventions and technology records">most significant technological achievements</a> of the 20th century, including the world's <a href="/wiki/Sputnik" class="mw-redirect" title="Sputnik">first human-made satellite</a> and the launching of the <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">first human in space</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> in 1991, the Russian SFSR reconstituted itself as the Russian Federation. In the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/1993_Russian_constitutional_crisis" title="1993 Russian constitutional crisis">constitutional crisis of 1993</a>, a new <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Russia" title="Constitution of Russia">constitution</a> was adopted, and Russia has since been governed as a <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federal</a> <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a> republic. <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> has dominated Russia's political system <a href="/wiki/2000_Russian_presidential_election" title="2000 Russian presidential election">since 2000</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russia_under_Vladimir_Putin" title="Russia under Vladimir Putin">his government</a> has been accused of <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarianism</a>, numerous <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Russia" title="Human rights in Russia">human rights abuses</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Russia" title="Corruption in Russia">corruption</a>. </p>
      <p>Russia is a <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">great power</a>, and is considered a <a href="/wiki/Potential_superpower" class="mw-redirect" title="Potential superpower">potential superpower</a>. It is ranked very high in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Russia" title="Healthcare in Russia">universal healthcare system</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Free_education" title="Free education">free</a> <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Russia" title="Education in Russia">university education</a>. Russia's <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Russia" title="Economy of Russia">economy</a> is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">eleventh-largest by nominal GDP</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">sixth-largest by PPP</a>. It is a recognised <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear weapons states">nuclear-weapons state</a>, possessing the world's <a href="/wiki/Russia_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Russia and weapons of mass destruction">largest stockpile of nuclear weapons</a>, with the world's <a href="/wiki/Military#Capability_development" title="Military">second-most powerful military</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditure" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by military expenditure">fourth-highest military expenditure</a>. Russia's extensive mineral and energy resources are the world's largest, and it is one of the leading <a href="/wiki/Oil_producer" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil producer">producers of oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_producer" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural gas producer">natural gas</a> globally. It is a <a href="/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council">permanent member</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>, a member of the <a href="/wiki/G-20_major_economies" class="mw-redirect" title="G-20 major economies">G20</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organisation">SCO</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific_Economic_Cooperation" title="Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation">APEC</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Investment_Bank" title="International Investment Bank">IIB</a> and the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a>, as well as the leading member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Collective_Security_Treaty_Organization" title="Collective Security Treaty Organization">CSTO</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Economic_Union" title="Eurasian Economic Union">EAEU</a>. Russia is also home to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Heritage_Sites_in_Russia" title="List of World Heritage Sites in Russia">ninth-greatest number</a> of <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Sites">World Heritage Sites</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Rus%27_people" title="Rus' people">Rus' people</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rus%27_(name)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rus' (name)">Rus' (name)</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Russian_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Russian (disambiguation)">Russian (disambiguation)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The name <i>Russia</i> is derived from <a href="/wiki/Rus%27_(name)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rus' (name)">Rus'</a>, a medieval state populated primarily by the <a href="/wiki/East_Slavs" title="East Slavs">East Slavs</a>. However, this proper name became more prominent in later history, and the country typically was called by its inhabitants "Ð ÑÑÑÐºÐ°Ñ Ð·ÐµÐ¼Ð»Ñ" (<i>Russkaya zemlya</i>), which can be translated as "Russian land" or "land of Rus." In order to distinguish this state from other states derived from it, it is denoted as <i><a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus'">Kievan Rus'</a></i> by modern historiography. The <a href="/wiki/Rus_(name)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rus (name)">name <i>Rus<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span></i></a> itself comes from the early medieval <a href="/wiki/Rus%27_people" title="Rus' people">Rus' people</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Swedes_(Germanic_tribe)" title="Swedes (Germanic tribe)">Swedish</a> merchants and warriors,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[13]</a></sup> who relocated from across the Baltic Sea and founded a state centred on <a href="/wiki/Novgorod" class="mw-redirect" title="Novgorod">Novgorod</a> that later became Kievan Rus'. </p>
      <p>An old Latin version of the name Rus' was <a href="/wiki/Ruthenia" title="Ruthenia">Ruthenia</a>, mostly applied to the western and southern regions of Rus' that were adjacent to Catholic Europe. The current name of the country, Ð Ð¾ÑÑÐ¸Ñ (<i>Rossiya</i>), comes from the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Greek" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine Greek">Byzantine Greek</a> designation of the <a href="/wiki/Rus%27_(name)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rus' (name)">Rus'</a>, Î¡ÏÏÏÎ¯Î± <i>RossÃ­a</i>âspelled Î¡ÏÏÎ¯Î± (<i>RosÃ­a</i> <small>pronounced&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Greek" title="Help:IPA/Greek">[roËsia]</a></span>) in <a href="/wiki/Modern_Greek" title="Modern Greek">Modern Greek</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[14]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The standard way to refer to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_nationality_law" title="Russian nationality law">citizens of Russia</a> is "Russians" in English.<sup id="cite_ref-merriamwebster_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-merriamwebster-18">[15]</a></sup> There are two words in <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> which are commonly translated into English as "Russians"âone is "ÑÑÑÑÐºÐ¸Ðµ" (<i>russkiye</i>), which most often refers to <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">ethnic Russians</a>âand the other is "ÑÐ¾ÑÑÐ¸ÑÐ½Ðµ" (<i>rossiyane</i>), which refers to the citizens of Russia, regardless of ethnicity.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[16]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Russia" title="History of Russia">History of Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Scythia" title="Scythia">Scythia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_colonies" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Greek colonies">Ancient Greek colonies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Early_Slavs" title="Early Slavs">Early Slavs</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Slavs" title="East Slavs">East Slavs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkic_expansion" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkic expansion">Turkic expansion</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Prehistory_of_Siberia" title="Prehistory of Siberia">Prehistory of Siberia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Indo-European">Proto-Indo-European</a> and <a href="/wiki/Proto-Uralic" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Uralic">Proto-Uralic</a>
      </div> 
      <p>One of the first <a href="/wiki/Cro-magnon" class="mw-redirect" title="Cro-magnon">modern human</a> bones of over 40,000 years old were found in Southern Russia, in the villages of <a href="/wiki/Kostyonki%E2%80%93Borshchyovo_archaeological_complex" title="KostyonkiâBorshchyovo archaeological complex">Kostyonki and Borshchyovo</a> situated on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Don_(river)" title="Don (river)">Don River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Nomadic_pastoralism" title="Nomadic pastoralism">Nomadic pastoralism</a> developed in the <a href="/wiki/Pontic%E2%80%93Caspian_steppe" title="PonticâCaspian steppe">PonticâCaspian steppe</a> beginning in the <a href="/wiki/Chalcolithic" title="Chalcolithic">Chalcolithic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Belinskij_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belinskij-22">[19]</a></sup> Remnants of these steppe civilizations were discovered in places such as <a href="/wiki/Ipatovo_kurgan" title="Ipatovo kurgan">Ipatovo</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Belinskij_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belinskij-22">[19]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sintashta" title="Sintashta">Sintashta</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[20]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arkaim" title="Arkaim">Arkaim</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[21]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Pazyryk_burials" title="Pazyryk burials">Pazyryk</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[22]</a></sup> which bear the earliest known traces of <a href="/wiki/Horses_in_warfare" title="Horses in warfare">horses in warfare</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a>, the Pontic-Caspian Steppe was known as <a href="/wiki/Scythia" title="Scythia">Scythia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Beginning in the 8th century BC, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Ancient Greek</a> traders brought their civilization to the trade emporiums located in the Russian cities of <a href="/wiki/Tanais" title="Tanais">Tanais</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phanagoria" title="Phanagoria">Phanagoria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 3rd to 4th centuries AD, the <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Gothic</a> kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Oium" title="Oium">Oium</a> existed in Southern Russia, which was later overrun by <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a>. Between the 3rd and 6th centuries AD, the <a href="/wiki/Bosporan_Kingdom" title="Bosporan Kingdom">Bosporan Kingdom</a>, which was a Hellenistic <a href="/wiki/Polity" title="Polity">polity</a> that succeeded the Greek colonies,<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[25]</a></sup> was also overwhelmed by nomadic invasions led by warlike tribes such as the Huns and <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Avars" title="Pannonian Avars">Eurasian Avars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[26]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Khazars" title="Khazars">Khazars</a>, who were of <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic origin</a>, ruled the lower <a href="/wiki/Volga" title="Volga">Volga</a> basin steppes between the Caspian and Black Seas until the 10th century.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The ancestors of modern <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> are the <a href="/wiki/List_of_ancient_Slavic_peoples" title="List of ancient Slavic peoples">Slavic tribes</a>, whose original home is thought by some scholars to have been the wooded areas of the <a href="/wiki/Pinsk_Marshes" title="Pinsk Marshes">Pinsk Marshes</a>, one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Wetland" title="Wetland">wetlands</a> in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[28]</a></sup> The East Slavs gradually settled Western Russia in two waves: one moving from <a href="/wiki/Kiev" class="mw-redirect" title="Kiev">Kiev</a> toward present-day <a href="/wiki/Suzdal" title="Suzdal">Suzdal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Murom" title="Murom">Murom</a> and another from <a href="/wiki/Polotsk" title="Polotsk">Polotsk</a> toward <a href="/wiki/Novgorod" class="mw-redirect" title="Novgorod">Novgorod</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rostov" title="Rostov">Rostov</a>. From the 7th century onwards, the East Slavs constituted the bulk of the population in Western Russia,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[29]</a></sup> and slowly but peacefully assimilated the native <a href="/wiki/Finno-Ugric_peoples" title="Finno-Ugric peoples">Finno-Ugric peoples</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Volga_Finns#Merya" title="Volga Finns">Merya</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[30]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Volga_Finns#Muroma" title="Volga Finns">Muromians</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[31]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Volga_Finns#Meshchera" title="Volga Finns">Meshchera</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Kievan_Rus.27"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Kievan_Rus'">Kievan Rus'</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Rus%27_Khaganate" title="Rus' Khaganate">Rus' Khaganate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus'">Kievan Rus'</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_early_East_Slavic_states" class="mw-redirect" title="List of early East Slavic states">List of early East Slavic states</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kievan_Rus_en.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Kievan_Rus_en.jpg/200px-Kievan_Rus_en.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Kievan_Rus_en.jpg/300px-Kievan_Rus_en.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Kievan_Rus_en.jpg/400px-Kievan_Rus_en.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1384" data-file-height="1368"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kievan_Rus_en.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus%27" title="Kievan Rus'">Kievan Rus'</a> in the 11th century
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The establishment of the first East Slavic states in the 9th century coincided with the arrival of <i><a href="/wiki/Varangians" title="Varangians">Varangians</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Vikings</a> who ventured along the waterways extending from the eastern Baltic <a href="/wiki/From_the_Varangians_to_the_Greeks" class="mw-redirect" title="From the Varangians to the Greeks">to the Black</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volga_trade_route" title="Volga trade route">Caspian</a> Seas.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[33]</a></sup> According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Primary_Chronicle" title="Primary Chronicle">Primary Chronicle</a></i>, a Varangian from the <a href="/wiki/Rus%27_people" title="Rus' people">Rus' people</a>, named <a href="/wiki/Rurik" title="Rurik">Rurik</a>, was elected ruler of <a href="/wiki/Novgorod" class="mw-redirect" title="Novgorod">Novgorod</a> in 862. In 882, his successor <a href="/wiki/Oleg_of_Novgorod" title="Oleg of Novgorod">Oleg</a> ventured south and conquered <a href="/wiki/Kiev" class="mw-redirect" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[34]</a></sup> which had been previously paying tribute to the <a href="/wiki/Khazars" title="Khazars">Khazars</a>. Oleg, Rurik's son <a href="/wiki/Igor_of_Kiev" title="Igor of Kiev">Igor</a> and Igor's son <a href="/wiki/Sviatoslav_I_of_Kiev" class="mw-redirect" title="Sviatoslav I of Kiev">Sviatoslav</a> subsequently subdued all local <a href="/wiki/East_Slavs" title="East Slavs">East Slavic</a> tribes to Kievan rule, destroyed the <a href="/wiki/Khazar_Khaganate" class="mw-redirect" title="Khazar Khaganate">Khazar Khaganate</a> and launched several military expeditions to <a href="/wiki/Paphlagonian_expedition_of_the_Rus%27" title="Paphlagonian expedition of the Rus'">Byzantium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caspian_expeditions_of_the_Rus%27" title="Caspian expeditions of the Rus'">Persia</a>. </p>
      <p>In the 10th to 11th centuries, Kievan Rus' became one of the largest and most prosperous states in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[35]</a></sup> The reigns of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_the_Great" title="Vladimir the Great">Vladimir the Great</a> (980â1015) and his son <a href="/wiki/Yaroslav_the_Wise" title="Yaroslav the Wise">Yaroslav the Wise</a> (1019â1054) constitute the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Age" title="Golden Age">Golden Age</a> of Kiev, which saw <a href="/wiki/Christianisation_of_Kievan_Rus%27" class="mw-redirect" title="Christianisation of Kievan Rus'">the acceptance of</a> <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christianity</a> from <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantium</a> and the creation of the first East Slavic written <a href="/wiki/Legal_code" class="mw-redirect" title="Legal code">legal code</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Russkaya_Pravda" title="Russkaya Pravda">Russkaya Pravda</a></i>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lebedev_baptism.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Lebedev_baptism.jpg/220px-Lebedev_baptism.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Lebedev_baptism.jpg/330px-Lebedev_baptism.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Lebedev_baptism.jpg/440px-Lebedev_baptism.jpg 2x" data-file-width="992" data-file-height="715"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lebedev_baptism.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><i>The <a href="/wiki/Baptism_of_Kievans" class="mw-redirect" title="Baptism of Kievans">Baptism of Kievans</a></i>, by <a href="/wiki/Klavdy_Lebedev" title="Klavdy Lebedev">Klavdy Lebedev</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the 11th and 12th centuries, constant incursions by nomadic Turkic tribes, such as the <a href="/wiki/Kipchaks" title="Kipchaks">Kipchaks</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pechenegs" title="Pechenegs">Pechenegs</a>, caused a massive migration of the East Slavic populations to the safer, heavily forested regions of the north, particularly to the area known as <a href="/wiki/Zalesye" title="Zalesye">Zalesye</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[36]</a></sup> which led to intermingling with the native <a href="/wiki/Volga_Finns" title="Volga Finns">Volga Finnic</a> tribes.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Curtis_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis-41">[38]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The age of <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">feudalism</a> and decentralization had come, marked by constant in-fighting between members of the <a href="/wiki/Rurikid_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Rurikid Dynasty">Rurikid Dynasty</a> that ruled Kievan Rus' collectively. Kiev's dominance waned, to the benefit of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir-Suzdal" title="Vladimir-Suzdal">Vladimir-Suzdal</a> in the north-east, <a href="/wiki/Novgorod_Republic" title="Novgorod Republic">Novgorod Republic</a> in the north-west and <a href="/wiki/Galicia-Volhynia" class="mw-redirect" title="Galicia-Volhynia">Galicia-Volhynia</a> in the south-west. </p>
      <p>Ultimately Kievan Rus' disintegrated, with the final blow being the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Kievan_Rus%27" title="Mongol invasion of Kievan Rus'">Mongol invasion</a> of 1237â40,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[39]</a></sup> that resulted in the destruction of Kiev,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[40]</a></sup> and the death of about half the population of Rus'.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[41]</a></sup> The invaders, later known as <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatars</a>, formed the state of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a>, which pillaged the Russian principalities and ruled the southern and central expanses of Russia for over two centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Galicia-Volhynia was eventually assimilated by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland_(1025%E2%80%931385)" title="Kingdom of Poland (1025â1385)">Kingdom of Poland</a>, while the Novgorod Republic and Mongol-dominated Vladimir-Suzdal, two regions on the periphery of Kiev, established the basis for the modern Russian nation.<sup id="cite_ref-Curtis_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Curtis-41">[38]</a></sup> The Novgorod Republic escaped Mongol occupation and together with <a href="/wiki/Pskov" title="Pskov">Pskov</a> retained some degree of autonomy during the time of the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_yoke" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongol yoke">Mongol yoke</a>; they were largely spared the atrocities that affected the rest of the country. Led by Prince <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Nevsky" title="Alexander Nevsky">Alexander Nevsky</a>, Novgorodians repelled the invading Swedes in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Neva" title="Battle of the Neva">Battle of the Neva</a> in 1240, as well as the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Crusades" title="Northern Crusades">Germanic crusaders</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Ice" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of the Ice">Battle of the Ice</a> in 1242. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_Duchy_of_Moscow">Grand Duchy of Moscow</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Moscow" title="Grand Duchy of Moscow">Grand Duchy of Moscow</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lissner_TroiceSergievaLavr.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Lissner_TroiceSergievaLavr.jpg/220px-Lissner_TroiceSergievaLavr.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Lissner_TroiceSergievaLavr.jpg/330px-Lissner_TroiceSergievaLavr.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Lissner_TroiceSergievaLavr.jpg/440px-Lissner_TroiceSergievaLavr.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2016" data-file-height="1400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lissner_TroiceSergievaLavr.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Sergius_of_Radonezh" title="Sergius of Radonezh">Sergius of Radonezh</a> blessing <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Donskoy" title="Dmitry Donskoy">Dmitry Donskoy</a> in <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Sergius_Lavra" class="mw-redirect" title="Trinity Sergius Lavra">Trinity Sergius Lavra</a>, before the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kulikovo" title="Battle of Kulikovo">Battle of Kulikovo</a>, depicted in a painting by <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Lissner" title="Ernst Lissner">Ernst Lissner</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The most powerful state to eventually arise after the destruction of Kievan Rus' was the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Moscow" title="Grand Duchy of Moscow">Grand Duchy of Moscow</a>, initially a part of <a href="/wiki/Vladimir-Suzdal" title="Vladimir-Suzdal">Vladimir-Suzdal</a>. While still under the domain of the <a href="/wiki/Mongol" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongol">Mongol</a>-<a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatars</a> and with their connivance, Moscow began to assert its influence in the Central Rus' in the early 14th century, gradually becoming the leading force in the process of the Rus' lands' reunification and expansion of Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[43]</a></sup> Moscow's last rival, the <a href="/wiki/Novgorod_Republic" title="Novgorod Republic">Novgorod Republic</a>, prospered as the chief <a href="/wiki/Fur_trade" title="Fur trade">fur trade</a> centre and the easternmost port of the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hanseatic League</a>. </p>
      <p>Times remained difficult, with frequent <a href="/wiki/Mongol-Tatar_raids" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongol-Tatar raids">Mongol-Tatar raids</a>. <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">Agriculture</a> suffered from the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Little_Ice_Age" title="Little Ice Age">Little Ice Age</a>. As in the rest of Europe, <a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">plague</a> was a frequent occurrence between 1350 and 1490.<sup id="cite_ref-Byrne_p.62_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Byrne_p.62-47">[44]</a></sup> However, because of the lower population density and better hygieneâwidespread practicing of <a href="/wiki/Banya_(sauna)" title="Banya (sauna)">banya</a>, a wet steam bathâthe death rate from plague was not as severe as in Western Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-banya_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-banya-48">[45]</a></sup> and population numbers recovered by 1500.<sup id="cite_ref-Byrne_p.62_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Byrne_p.62-47">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Led by Prince <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Donskoy" title="Dmitry Donskoy">Dmitry Donskoy</a> of Moscow and helped by the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a>, the united army of Russian principalities inflicted a milestone defeat on the Mongol-Tatars in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kulikovo" title="Battle of Kulikovo">Battle of Kulikovo</a> in 1380. Moscow gradually absorbed the surrounding principalities, including formerly strong rivals such as <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Tver" title="Principality of Tver">Tver</a> and <a href="/wiki/Novgorod_Republic" title="Novgorod Republic">Novgorod</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ivan_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivan III">Ivan&nbsp;III</a> ("the Great") finally threw off the control of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a> and consolidated the whole of Central and Northern Rus' under Moscow's dominion. He was also the first to take the title "Grand Duke of all the Russias".<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[46]</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">fall of Constantinople</a> in 1453, Moscow <a href="/wiki/Third_Rome" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Rome">claimed succession to the legacy</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Roman Empire">Eastern Roman Empire</a>. Ivan&nbsp;III married <a href="/wiki/Sophia_Palaiologina" title="Sophia Palaiologina">Sophia Palaiologina</a>, the niece of the last <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Emperor" class="mw-redirect" title="Byzantine Emperor">Byzantine Emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Constantine_XI" class="mw-redirect" title="Constantine XI">Constantine&nbsp;XI</a>, and made the Byzantine <a href="/wiki/Double-headed_eagle" title="Double-headed eagle">double-headed eagle</a> his own, and eventually Russia's, coat-of-arms. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tsardom_of_Russia">Tsardom of Russia</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia">Tsardom of Russia</a>
      </div>
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Moscow,_third_Rome" title="Moscow, third Rome">Moscow, third Rome</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vasnetsov_Ioann_4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Vasnetsov_Ioann_4.jpg/150px-Vasnetsov_Ioann_4.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="281" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Vasnetsov_Ioann_4.jpg/225px-Vasnetsov_Ioann_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Vasnetsov_Ioann_4.jpg/300px-Vasnetsov_Ioann_4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="2996"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vasnetsov_Ioann_4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tsar <a href="/wiki/Ivan_the_Terrible" title="Ivan the Terrible">Ivan the Terrible</a>, 19th-century evocation by <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Vasnetsov" title="Viktor Vasnetsov">Viktor Vasnetsov</a>, 1897
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In development of the <a href="/wiki/Third_Rome" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Rome">Third Rome</a> ideas, the Grand Duke <a href="/wiki/Ivan_IV" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivan IV">Ivan&nbsp;IV</a> (the "Terrible") was officially crowned first <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia"><i>Tsar</i></a> of Russia in 1547. The <i>Tsar</i> <a href="/wiki/Promulgation" title="Promulgation">promulgated</a> a new code of laws (<a href="/wiki/Sudebnik_of_1550" title="Sudebnik of 1550">Sudebnik of 1550</a>), established the first Russian feudal representative body (<a href="/wiki/Zemsky_Sobor" title="Zemsky Sobor">Zemsky Sobor</a>) and introduced local self-management into the rural regions.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During his long reign, Ivan the Terrible nearly doubled the already large Russian territory by annexing the three Tatar khanates (parts of the disintegrated <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a>): <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Kazan" title="Khanate of Kazan">Kazan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Astrakhan_Khanate" title="Astrakhan Khanate">Astrakhan</a> along the <a href="/wiki/Volga_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Volga River">Volga River</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Siberian_Khanate" class="mw-redirect" title="Siberian Khanate">Siberian Khanate</a> in southwestern Siberia. Thus, by the end of the 16th century, Russia expanded into Asia, and was transformed into a <a href="/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries" title="List of transcontinental countries">transcontinental state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>However, the Tsardom was weakened by the long and unsuccessful <a href="/wiki/Livonian_War" title="Livonian War">Livonian War</a> against the coalition of Poland, Lithuania, and Sweden for access to the Baltic coast and sea trade.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup> At the same time, the Tatars of the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Crimean Khanate</a>, the only remaining successor to the Golden Horde, continued to raid Southern Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[51]</a></sup> In an effort to restore the Volga khanates, Crimeans and their <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> allies <a href="/wiki/Russo-Crimean_Wars" title="Russo-Crimean Wars">invaded central Russia</a> and were even able to <a href="/wiki/Fire_of_Moscow_(1571)" title="Fire of Moscow (1571)">burn down parts of Moscow</a> in 1571.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup> But in the next year the large invading army was thoroughly defeated by Russians in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Molodi" title="Battle of Molodi">Battle of Molodi</a>, forever eliminating the threat of an OttomanâCrimean expansion into Russia. The <a href="/wiki/Crimean-Nogai_raids_into_East_Slavic_lands" class="mw-redirect" title="Crimean-Nogai raids into East Slavic lands">slave raids of Crimeans</a>, however, did not cease until the late 17th century though the construction of new fortification lines across Southern Russia, such as the <a href="/wiki/Great_Abatis_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Abatis Line">Great Abatis Line</a>, constantly narrowed the area accessible to incursions.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Appeal_of_Minin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Appeal_of_Minin.jpg/170px-Appeal_of_Minin.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Appeal_of_Minin.jpg/255px-Appeal_of_Minin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Appeal_of_Minin.jpg/340px-Appeal_of_Minin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2039" data-file-height="2400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Appeal_of_Minin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Kuzma_Minin" title="Kuzma Minin">Kuzma Minin</a> appeals to the people of <a href="/wiki/Nizhny_Novgorod" title="Nizhny Novgorod">Nizhny Novgorod</a> to raise a volunteer army against the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Muscovite_War_(1605%E2%80%9318)" class="mw-redirect" title="PolishâMuscovite War (1605â18)">Polish invaders</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The death of Ivan's sons marked the end of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Rurik_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Rurik Dynasty">Rurik Dynasty</a> in 1598, and in combination with the <a href="/wiki/Russian_famine_of_1601%E2%80%9303" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian famine of 1601â03">famine of 1601â03</a>, led to a civil war, the rule of pretenders, and foreign intervention during the <a href="/wiki/Time_of_Troubles" title="Time of Troubles">Time of Troubles</a> in the early 17th century.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="PolishâLithuanian Commonwealth">PolishâLithuanian Commonwealth</a> occupied parts of Russia, including Moscow. In 1612, the Poles were forced to retreat by the Russian volunteer corps, led by two national heroes, merchant <a href="/wiki/Kuzma_Minin" title="Kuzma Minin">Kuzma Minin</a> and Prince <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Pozharsky" title="Dmitry Pozharsky">Dmitry Pozharsky</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Romanov_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanov Dynasty">Romanov Dynasty</a> acceded to the throne in 1613 by the decision of Zemsky Sobor, and the country started its gradual recovery from the crisis. </p>
      <p>Russia continued its territorial growth through the 17th century, which was the age of <a href="/wiki/Cossacks" title="Cossacks">Cossacks</a>. In 1648, the peasants of Ukraine joined the <a href="/wiki/Zaporozhian_Cossacks" title="Zaporozhian Cossacks">Zaporozhian Cossacks</a> in rebellion against Poland-Lithuania during the <a href="/wiki/Khmelnytsky_Uprising" title="Khmelnytsky Uprising">Khmelnytsky Uprising</a> in reaction to the social and religious oppression they had been suffering under Polish rule. In 1654, the Ukrainian leader, <a href="/wiki/Bohdan_Khmelnytsky" title="Bohdan Khmelnytsky">Bohdan Khmelnytsky</a>, offered to place Ukraine under the protection of the Russian Tsar, <a href="/wiki/Aleksey_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Aleksey I">Aleksey&nbsp;I</a>. Aleksey's acceptance of this offer led to another <a href="/wiki/Russo-Polish_War_(1654%E2%80%931667)" title="Russo-Polish War (1654â1667)">Russo-Polish War</a>. Finally, Ukraine was split along the <a href="/wiki/Dnieper_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Dnieper River">Dnieper River</a>, leaving the western part, <a href="/wiki/Right-bank_Ukraine" title="Right-bank Ukraine">right-bank Ukraine</a>, under Polish rule and the eastern part (<a href="/wiki/Left-bank_Ukraine" title="Left-bank Ukraine">Left-bank Ukraine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kiev" class="mw-redirect" title="Kiev">Kiev</a>) under Russian rule. Later, in 1670â71, the <a href="/wiki/Don_Cossacks" title="Don Cossacks">Don Cossacks</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Stenka_Razin" title="Stenka Razin">Stenka Razin</a> initiated a major uprising in the <a href="/wiki/Volga_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Volga Region">Volga Region</a>, but the Tsar's troops were successful in defeating the rebels.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the east, the rapid Russian exploration and colonisation of the huge territories of Siberia was led mostly by Cossacks hunting for valuable furs and ivory. <a href="/wiki/List_of_Russian_explorers" title="List of Russian explorers">Russian explorers</a> pushed eastward primarily along the <a href="/wiki/Siberian_River_Routes" title="Siberian River Routes">Siberian River Routes</a>, and by the mid-17th century, there were Russian settlements in Eastern Siberia, on the <a href="/wiki/Chukchi_Peninsula" title="Chukchi Peninsula">Chukchi Peninsula</a>, along the <a href="/wiki/Amur_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Amur River">Amur River</a>, and on the Pacific coast. In 1648, <a href="/wiki/Fedot_Popov" class="mw-redirect" title="Fedot Popov">Fedot Popov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semyon_Dezhnyov" class="mw-redirect" title="Semyon Dezhnyov">Semyon Dezhnyov</a>, two Russian explorers, discovered the <a href="/wiki/Bering_Strait" title="Bering Strait">Bering Strait</a>; which led to the Russians becoming the first Europeans to sail to North America.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperial_Russia">Imperial Russia</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Peter_I_by_Kneller.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Peter_I_by_Kneller.jpg/170px-Peter_I_by_Kneller.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="281" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Peter_I_by_Kneller.jpg/255px-Peter_I_by_Kneller.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Peter_I_by_Kneller.jpg/340px-Peter_I_by_Kneller.jpg 2x" data-file-width="906" data-file-height="1500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Peter_I_by_Kneller.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tsar_of_All_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Tsar of All Russia">Tsar of All Russia</a> in 1682â1721 and the first <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_All_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Emperor of All Russia">Emperor of All Russia</a> in 1721â1725
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Under <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">Peter the Great</a>, Russia was proclaimed an Empire in 1721, and became recognised as a global power. Ruling from 1682 to 1725, Peter defeated Sweden in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War" title="Great Northern War">Great Northern War</a>, forcing it to cede West <a href="/wiki/Karelia" title="Karelia">Karelia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ingria" title="Ingria">Ingria</a> (two regions lost by Russia in the <a href="/wiki/Time_of_Troubles" title="Time of Troubles">Time of Troubles</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[57]</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/Governorate_of_Estonia" title="Governorate of Estonia">Estland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Livland" class="mw-redirect" title="Livland">Livland</a>, securing Russia's access to the sea and sea trade.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[58]</a></sup> On the Baltic Sea, Peter founded a new capital named <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a>. Later, <a href="/wiki/Government_reform_of_Peter_the_Great" title="Government reform of Peter the Great">his reforms</a> brought considerable Western European cultural influences to Russia. </p>
      <p>The reign of Peter&nbsp;I's daughter <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_of_Russia" title="Elizabeth of Russia">Elizabeth</a> in 1741â62 saw Russia's participation in the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> (1756â63). During this conflict, Russia annexed <a href="/wiki/East_Prussia" title="East Prussia">East Prussia</a> for a while and even took Berlin. However, upon Elizabeth's death, all these conquests were returned to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Kingdom of Prussia</a> by pro-Prussian <a href="/wiki/Peter_III_of_Russia" title="Peter III of Russia">Peter&nbsp;III of Russia</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine&nbsp;II</a> ("the Great"), who ruled in 1762â96, presided over the Age of <a href="/wiki/Russian_Enlightenment" title="Russian Enlightenment">Russian Enlightenment</a>. She extended Russian political control over the Polish-Lithuanian Commonwealth and incorporated most of its territories into Russia during the <a href="/wiki/Partitions_of_Poland" title="Partitions of Poland">Partitions of Poland</a>, pushing the Russian frontier westward into Central Europe. In the south, after the successful <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_Wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Russo-Turkish Wars">Russo-Turkish Wars</a> against <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkey" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottoman Turkey">Ottoman Turkey</a>, Catherine advanced Russia's boundary to the Black Sea, defeating the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Crimean Khanate</a>. As a result of victories over <a href="/wiki/Qajar_dynasty" title="Qajar dynasty">Qajar Iran</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Persian_Wars" title="Russo-Persian Wars">Russo-Persian Wars</a>, by the first half of the 19th century, Russia also made significant territorial gains in <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasia" title="Transcaucasia">Transcaucasia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/North_Caucasus" title="North Caucasus">North Caucasus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[60]</a></sup> Catherine's successor, her son <a href="/wiki/Paul_I_of_Russia" title="Paul I of Russia">Paul</a>, was <a href="/wiki/Personality_and_reputation_of_Paul_I_of_Russia" title="Personality and reputation of Paul I of Russia">unstable and focused predominantly on domestic issues</a>. Following his short reign, Catherine's strategy was continued with <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia" title="Alexander I of Russia">Alexander&nbsp;I's</a> (1801â25) wresting of Finland from the weakened kingdom of Sweden in 1809 and of <a href="/wiki/Bessarabia" title="Bessarabia">Bessarabia</a> from the Ottomans in 1812. At the same time, Russians became the first Europeans to <a href="/wiki/Russian_America" title="Russian America">colonise Alaska</a> and founded settlements in California, such as <a href="/wiki/Fort_Ross" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort Ross">Fort Ross</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Territorial_Expansion_of_Russia.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Territorial_Expansion_of_Russia.svg/220px-Territorial_Expansion_of_Russia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Territorial_Expansion_of_Russia.svg/330px-Territorial_Expansion_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Territorial_Expansion_of_Russia.svg/440px-Territorial_Expansion_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="1511"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Territorial_Expansion_of_Russia.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Russian <a href="/wiki/Expansion_of_Russia_(1500%E2%80%931800)" title="Expansion of Russia (1500â1800)">expansion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_Russia" title="Territorial evolution of Russia">territorial evolution</a> between the 14th and 20th centuries
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1803â1806, the <a href="/wiki/First_Russian_circumnavigation" title="First Russian circumnavigation">first Russian circumnavigation</a> was made, later followed by other notable Russian sea exploration voyages. In 1820, <a href="/wiki/Fabian_Gottlieb_von_Bellingshausen#First_Russian_Antarctic_expedition" title="Fabian Gottlieb von Bellingshausen">a Russian expedition</a> discovered the continent of <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a>. </p>
      <p>In alliances with various other European countries, Russia fought against <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>'s France. The <a href="/wiki/French_invasion_of_Russia" title="French invasion of Russia">French invasion of Russia</a> at the height of Napoleon's power in 1812 reached Moscow, but eventually failed miserably as the obstinate resistance in combination with the bitterly cold <a href="/wiki/Russian_winter" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian winter">Russian winter</a> led to a disastrous defeat of invaders, in which more than 95% of the pan-European <a href="/wiki/Grande_Arm%C3%A9e" title="Grande ArmÃ©e">Grande ArmÃ©e</a> perished.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[61]</a></sup> Led by <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Kutuzov" title="Mikhail Kutuzov">Mikhail Kutuzov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barclay_de_Tolly" title="Barclay de Tolly">Barclay de Tolly</a>, the Russian army ousted Napoleon from the country and drove throughout Europe in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Sixth_Coalition" title="War of the Sixth Coalition">war of the Sixth Coalition</a>, finally entering Paris. Alexander&nbsp;I headed Russia's delegation at the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a> that defined the map of post-Napoleonic Europe. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koetoezov_kazan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Koetoezov_kazan.jpg/180px-Koetoezov_kazan.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="270" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Koetoezov_kazan.jpg/270px-Koetoezov_kazan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Koetoezov_kazan.jpg/360px-Koetoezov_kazan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koetoezov_kazan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Monument to <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Kutuzov" title="Mikhail Kutuzov">Mikhail Kutuzov</a> in front of the <a href="/wiki/Kazan_Cathedral,_St._Petersburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazan Cathedral, St. Petersburg">Kazan Cathedral</a> in Saint Petersburg. The Kazan Cathedral and the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Christ_the_Saviour" title="Cathedral of Christ the Saviour">Cathedral of Christ the Saviour</a> in Moscow were built to commemorate <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>'s defeat.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The officers of the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> brought ideas of liberalism back to Russia with them and attempted to curtail the tsar's powers during the abortive <a href="/wiki/Decembrist_revolt" title="Decembrist revolt">Decembrist revolt</a> of 1825. At the end of the conservative reign of <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicolas I">Nicolas&nbsp;I</a> (1825â55), a zenith period of Russia's power and influence in Europe was disrupted by defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a>. Between 1847 and 1851, about one million people died of Asiatic <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Nicholas's successor <a href="/wiki/Alexander_II_of_Russia" title="Alexander II of Russia">Alexander&nbsp;II</a> (1855â81) enacted significant changes in the country, including the <a href="/wiki/Emancipation_reform_of_1861" title="Emancipation reform of 1861">emancipation reform of 1861</a>. These <i>Great Reforms</i> spurred industrialisation and modernised the Russian army, which had successfully liberated Bulgaria from Ottoman rule in the <a href="/wiki/1877%E2%80%9378_Russo-Turkish_War" class="mw-redirect" title="1877â78 Russo-Turkish War">1877â78 Russo-Turkish War</a>. </p>
      <p>The late 19th century saw the rise of various socialist movements in Russia. Alexander&nbsp;II was killed in 1881 by revolutionary terrorists and the reign of his son <a href="/wiki/Alexander_III_of_Russia" title="Alexander III of Russia">Alexander&nbsp;III</a> (1881â94) was less liberal but more peaceful. The last Russian Emperor, <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Nicholas II">Nicholas&nbsp;II</a> (1894â1917), was unable to prevent the events of the Russian <a href="/wiki/Revolution_of_1905" class="mw-redirect" title="Revolution of 1905">Revolution of 1905</a>, triggered by the unsuccessful <a href="/wiki/Russo-Japanese_War" title="Russo-Japanese War">Russo-Japanese War</a> and the demonstration incident known as <a href="/wiki/Bloody_Sunday_(1905)" title="Bloody Sunday (1905)">Bloody Sunday</a>. The uprising was put down, but the government was forced to concede major reforms (<a href="/wiki/Russian_Constitution_of_1906" title="Russian Constitution of 1906">Russian Constitution of 1906</a>), including granting the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedoms of speech</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_assembly" title="Freedom of assembly">assembly</a>, the legalisation of political parties, and the creation of an elected legislative body, the <a href="/wiki/State_Duma_of_the_Russian_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="State Duma of the Russian Empire">State Duma of the Russian Empire</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Stolypin_reform" title="Stolypin reform">Stolypin agrarian reform</a> led to a massive peasant migration and settlement into <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>. More than four million settlers arrived in that region between 1906 and 1914.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="February_Revolution_and_Russian_Republic">February Revolution and Russian Republic</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/February_Revolution" title="February Revolution">February Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Provisional_Government" title="Russian Provisional Government">Russian Provisional Government</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Republic" title="Russian Republic">Russian Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/1917_Russian_Constituent_Assembly_election" title="1917 Russian Constituent Assembly election">1917 Russian Constituent Assembly election</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Democratic_Federative_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Democratic Federative Republic">Russian Democratic Federative Republic</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Russian_Imperial_Family_1913.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Russian_Imperial_Family_1913.jpg/220px-Russian_Imperial_Family_1913.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Russian_Imperial_Family_1913.jpg/330px-Russian_Imperial_Family_1913.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Russian_Imperial_Family_1913.jpg/440px-Russian_Imperial_Family_1913.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3711" data-file-height="3281"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Russian_Imperial_Family_1913.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Emperor <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia" title="Nicholas II of Russia">Nicholas II of Russia</a> and his family <a href="/wiki/Execution_of_the_Romanov_family" title="Execution of the Romanov family">were murdered</a> by the Bolsheviks in 1918.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1914, Russia entered <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War&nbsp;I</a> in response to <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>'s declaration of war on Russia's ally <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbia" title="Kingdom of Serbia">Serbia</a>, and fought across multiple fronts while isolated from its <a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">Triple Entente</a> allies. In 1916, the <a href="/wiki/Brusilov_Offensive" class="mw-redirect" title="Brusilov Offensive">Brusilov Offensive</a> of the Russian Army almost completely destroyed the military of Austria-Hungary. However, the already-existing public distrust of the regime was deepened by the rising costs of war, <a href="/wiki/World_War_I_casualties" title="World War I casualties">high casualties</a>, and rumors of corruption and treason. All this formed the climate for the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a> of 1917, carried out in two major acts. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/February_Revolution" title="February Revolution">February Revolution</a> forced <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia" title="Nicholas II of Russia">Nicholas II</a> to abdicate; he and his family were imprisoned and <a href="/wiki/Shooting_of_the_Romanov_family" class="mw-redirect" title="Shooting of the Romanov family">later executed in Yekaterinburg</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a>. The monarchy was replaced by a shaky coalition of political parties that declared itself the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Provisional_Government" title="Russian Provisional Government">Provisional Government</a>. On 1 September (14), 1917, upon a decree of the Provisional Government, the Russian Republic was proclaimed.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[64]</a></sup> On 6 January (19), 1918, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Constituent_Assembly" title="Russian Constituent Assembly">Russian Constituent Assembly</a> declared Russia a democratic federal republic (thus ratifying the Provisional Government's decision). The next day the Constituent Assembly was dissolved by the <a href="/wiki/All-Russian_Central_Executive_Committee" title="All-Russian Central Executive Committee">All-Russian Central Executive Committee</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_Civil_War">Russian Civil War</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a>, and <a href="/wiki/White_movement" title="White movement">White movement</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Russia_Constitution_of_1918" title="Soviet Russia Constitution of 1918">Soviet Russia Constitution of 1918</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Thecristisrizenoldrussiancivilwarposter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Thecristisrizenoldrussiancivilwarposter.jpg/180px-Thecristisrizenoldrussiancivilwarposter.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Thecristisrizenoldrussiancivilwarposter.jpg/270px-Thecristisrizenoldrussiancivilwarposter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Thecristisrizenoldrussiancivilwarposter.jpg/360px-Thecristisrizenoldrussiancivilwarposter.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="1766"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Thecristisrizenoldrussiancivilwarposter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>1932 <a href="/wiki/White_%C3%A9migr%C3%A9" title="White Ã©migrÃ©">White Ã©migrÃ©</a> propaganda poster
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>An alternative socialist establishment co-existed, the <a href="/wiki/Petrograd_Soviet" title="Petrograd Soviet">Petrograd Soviet</a>, wielding power through the democratically elected councils of workers and peasants, called <i><a href="/wiki/Soviet_(council)" title="Soviet (council)">Soviets</a></i>. The rule of the new authorities only aggravated the crisis in the country instead of resolving it. Eventually, the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a>, led by <a href="/wiki/Bolshevik" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik">Bolshevik</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a>, overthrew the Provisional Government and gave full governing power to the Soviets, leading to the creation of the world's first <a href="/wiki/Socialist_state" title="Socialist state">socialist state</a>. </p>
      <p>Following the October Revolution, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a> broke out between the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Communist" class="mw-redirect" title="Anti-Communist">anti-Communist</a> <a href="/wiki/White_movement" title="White movement">White movement</a> and the new <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_council" title="Workers' council">Soviet</a> regime with its <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a>. Bolshevist Russia lost its Ukrainian, Polish, Baltic, and Finnish territories by signing the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Brest-Litovsk_(Russia%E2%80%93Central_Powers)" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Brest-Litovsk (RussiaâCentral Powers)">Treaty of Brest-Litovsk</a> that concluded hostilities with the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> of World War&nbsp;I. The <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I" title="Allies of World War I">Allied powers</a> launched an unsuccessful <a href="/wiki/Allied_intervention_in_the_Russian_Civil_War" title="Allied intervention in the Russian Civil War">military intervention</a> in support of anti-Communist forces. In the meantime, both the Bolsheviks and White movement carried out campaigns of deportations and executions against each other, known respectively as the <a href="/wiki/Red_Terror" title="Red Terror">Red Terror</a> and <a href="/wiki/White_Terror_(Russia)" title="White Terror (Russia)">White Terror</a>. By the end of the civil war, Russia's economy and infrastructure were heavily damaged. There were an estimated 7â12 million casualties during the war, mostly civilians.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[65]</a></sup> Millions became <a href="/wiki/White_%C3%A9migr%C3%A9" title="White Ã©migrÃ©">White Ã©migrÃ©s</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[66]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_famine_of_1921%E2%80%9322" title="Russian famine of 1921â22">Russian famine of 1921â22</a> claimed up to five&nbsp;million victims.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[67]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_Union">Soviet Union</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="History of the Soviet Union">History of the Soviet Union</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Creation_of_the_USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty on the Creation of the USSR">Treaty on the Creation of the USSR</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Stalin-Lenin-Kalinin-1919.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Stalin-Lenin-Kalinin-1919.jpg/170px-Stalin-Lenin-Kalinin-1919.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="88" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Stalin-Lenin-Kalinin-1919.jpg/255px-Stalin-Lenin-Kalinin-1919.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Stalin-Lenin-Kalinin-1919.jpg/340px-Stalin-Lenin-Kalinin-1919.jpg 2x" data-file-width="880" data-file-height="456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Stalin-Lenin-Kalinin-1919.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Kalinin" title="Mikhail Kalinin">Mikhail Kalinin</a> meeting in 1919.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 30 December 1922, Lenin and his aides <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Creation_of_the_USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty on the Creation of the USSR">formed</a> the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, by merging the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian SFSR</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Ukrainian SSR">Ukrainian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byelorussian_SSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Byelorussian SSR">Byelorussian</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Transcaucasian_Socialist_Federative_Soviet_Republic" title="Transcaucasian Socialist Federative Soviet Republic">Transcaucasian SFSR</a>. Out of the 15 <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">republics of the Soviet Union</a>, the largest in size and population was the Russian SFSR, which dominated the union for its entire history politically, culturally, and economically. </p>
      <p>Following <a href="/wiki/Death_and_state_funeral_of_Vladimir_Lenin" title="Death and state funeral of Vladimir Lenin">Lenin's death</a> in 1924, a <a href="/wiki/List_of_leaders_of_the_Soviet_Union#List_of_troikas" title="List of leaders of the Soviet Union">troika</a> was designated to take charge. Eventually <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="General Secretary of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union">General Secretary of the Communist Party</a>, managed to suppress all opposition factions and consolidate power in his hands to become the country's dictator by the 1930s. <a href="/wiki/Leon_Trotsky" title="Leon Trotsky">Leon Trotsky</a>, the main proponent of <a href="/wiki/World_revolution" title="World revolution">world revolution</a>, was exiled from the Soviet Union in 1929, and Stalin's idea of <a href="/wiki/Socialism_in_One_Country" class="mw-redirect" title="Socialism in One Country">Socialism in One Country</a> became the official line. The continued internal struggle in the Bolshevik party culminated in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Purge" title="Great Purge">Great Purge</a>, a period of mass repressions in 1937â38, during which hundreds of thousands of people were executed, including <a href="/wiki/Old_Bolshevik" title="Old Bolshevik">original party members</a> and military leaders forced to confess to nonexistent plots.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Under Stalin's leadership, the government launched a <a href="/wiki/Command_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Command economy">command economy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Industrialization_in_the_USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrialization in the USSR">industrialisation of the largely rural country</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Collectivization_in_the_USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Collectivization in the USSR">collectivisation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_the_USSR" class="mw-redirect" title="Agriculture in the USSR">its agriculture</a>. During this period of rapid economic and social change, millions of people were sent to <a href="/wiki/Gulag" title="Gulag">penal labor camps</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Getty_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Getty-72">[69]</a></sup> including many political convicts for their suspected or real opposition to Stalin's rule; millions were <a href="/wiki/Population_transfer_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Population transfer in the Soviet Union">deported and exiled</a> to remote areas of the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-Getty_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Getty-72">[69]</a></sup> The transitional disorganisation of the country's agriculture, combined with the harsh state policies and a drought, led to the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_famine_of_1932%E2%80%931933" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet famine of 1932â1933">Soviet famine of 1932â1933</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[70]</a></sup> which killed between 2 and 3 million people in the Russian SFSR.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[71]</a></sup> The Soviet Union made the costly transformation from a largely agrarian economy to a major industrial powerhouse in a short span of time.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[72]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg/290px-RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg" decoding="async" width="290" height="104" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg/435px-RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg/580px-RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2163" data-file-height="776"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_44732_Soviet_soldiers_attack_house.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad" title="Battle of Stalingrad">Battle of Stalingrad</a>, the largest and bloodiest battle in the history of warfare, ended in 1943 with a decisive Soviet victory against the <a href="/wiki/German_Army_(1935%E2%80%931945)" title="German Army (1935â1945)">German Army</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 22 June 1941, Nazi Germany broke their non-aggression treaty; and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">invaded</a> the ill-prepared Soviet Union with the largest and most powerful invasion force in human history,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[73]</a></sup> opening the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">largest theater of World War&nbsp;II</a>. The Nazi <a href="/wiki/Hunger_Plan" title="Hunger Plan">Hunger Plan</a> foresaw the "extinction of industry as well as a great part of the population".<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[74]</a></sup> Nearly 3 million <a href="/wiki/German_mistreatment_of_Soviet_prisoners_of_war" title="German mistreatment of Soviet prisoners of war">Soviet POWs</a> in German captivity were murdered in just eight months of 1941â42.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[75]</a></sup> Although the <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a> had considerable early success, their attack was halted in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Moscow" title="Battle of Moscow">Battle of Moscow</a>. Subsequently, the Germans were dealt major defeats first at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad" title="Battle of Stalingrad">Battle of Stalingrad</a> in the winter of 1942â43,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[76]</a></sup> and then in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kursk" title="Battle of Kursk">Battle of Kursk</a> in the summer of 1943. Another German failure was the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Leningrad" title="Siege of Leningrad">Siege of Leningrad</a>, in which the city was fully blockaded on land between 1941 and 1944 by German and Finnish forces, and suffered starvation and more than a million deaths, but never surrendered.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[77]</a></sup> Under Stalin's administration and the leadership of such commanders as <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Zhukov" title="Georgy Zhukov">Georgy Zhukov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Rokossovsky" title="Konstantin Rokossovsky">Konstantin Rokossovsky</a>, Soviet forces steamrolled through Eastern and Central Europe in 1944â45 and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin" title="Battle of Berlin">captured Berlin</a> in May 1945. In August 1945 the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Army" title="Soviet Army">Soviet Army</a> <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Japanese_War" title="SovietâJapanese War">ousted the Japanese</a> from China's <a href="/wiki/Manchukuo" title="Manchukuo">Manchukuo</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, contributing to the allied victory over Japan. </p>
      <p>The 1941â45 period of World War&nbsp;II is known in Russia as the "<a href="/wiki/Great_Patriotic_War_(term)" title="Great Patriotic War (term)">Great Patriotic War</a>."
