The Soviet Union together with the United States, the United Kingdom and China were considered as the <a href="/wiki/Big_Four_in_World_War_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Four in World War II">Big Four</a> of Allied powers in World War II,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[78]</a></sup> and later became the <a href="/wiki/Four_Policemen" title="Four Policemen">Four Policemen</a> which was the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[79]</a></sup> During this war, which included many of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_battles_by_casualties" title="List of battles by casualties">most lethal battle operations</a> in human history, <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_casualties_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="World War II casualties of the Soviet Union">Soviet civilian and military death were about 27 million</a>, accounting for about a third of all <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_casualties" title="World War II casualties">World War&nbsp;II casualties</a>. The full demographic loss of Soviet citizens was even greater.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[80]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Economy of the Soviet Union">Soviet economy</a> and infrastructure suffered massive devastation, which caused the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_famine_of_1946%E2%80%9347" title="Soviet famine of 1946â47">Soviet famine of 1946â47</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[81]</a></sup> Nonetheless, the Soviet Union emerged as a global <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpower</a> in the aftermath.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[82]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_War">Cold War</span></h4> 
      <p>After World War II, Eastern and Central Europe, including <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a> and eastern parts of <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> were occupied by <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> according to the <a href="/wiki/Potsdam_Conference" title="Potsdam Conference">Potsdam Conference</a>. Dependent socialist governments were installed in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> satellite states. After becoming the world's second <a href="/wiki/Russia_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Russia and weapons of mass destruction">nuclear power</a>, the Soviet Union established the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> alliance and entered into a struggle for global dominance, known as the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, with the rivaling United States and <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>. </p>
      <p>After <a href="/wiki/Stalin%27s_death" class="mw-redirect" title="Stalin's death">Stalin's death</a> and a short period of <a href="/wiki/Collective_leadership" title="Collective leadership">collective rule</a>, the new leader <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a> denounced <a href="/wiki/On_the_Cult_of_Personality_and_Its_Consequences" title="On the Cult of Personality and Its Consequences">Stalin</a> and launched the policy of <a href="/wiki/De-Stalinisation" class="mw-redirect" title="De-Stalinisation">de-Stalinisation</a>. The penal labor system was reformed and many prisoners were released and rehabilitated (many of them posthumously).<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[83]</a></sup> The general easement of repressive policies became known later as the <a href="/wiki/Khrushchev_Thaw" title="Khrushchev Thaw">Khrushchev Thaw</a>. At the same time, tensions with the United States heightened when the two rivals clashed over the deployment of the United States <a href="/wiki/PGM-19_Jupiter" title="PGM-19 Jupiter">Jupiter missiles</a> in Turkey and Soviet <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Missile_Crisis" title="Cuban Missile Crisis">missiles in Cuba</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sputnik_asm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Sputnik_asm.jpg/220px-Sputnik_asm.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Sputnik_asm.jpg/330px-Sputnik_asm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Sputnik_asm.jpg/440px-Sputnik_asm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1094" data-file-height="896"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sputnik_asm.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Sputnik_1" title="Sputnik 1">Sputnik&nbsp;1</a> was the world's first artificial satellite.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1957, the Soviet Union launched the world's first artificial <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sputnik_1" title="Sputnik 1">Sputnik&nbsp;1</a></i>, thus starting the <a href="/wiki/Space_Age" title="Space Age">Space Age</a>. Russian <a href="/wiki/Cosmonaut" class="mw-redirect" title="Cosmonaut">cosmonaut</a> <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">Yuri Gagarin</a> became the first human to orbit the Earth, aboard the <i><a href="/wiki/Vostok_1" title="Vostok 1">Vostok&nbsp;1</a></i> manned spacecraft on <a href="/wiki/Cosmonautics_Day" title="Cosmonautics Day">12 April 1961</a>. Following the ousting of Khrushchev in 1964, another period of <a href="/wiki/Collectivity_of_leadership" class="mw-redirect" title="Collectivity of leadership">collective rule</a> ensued, until <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev" title="Leonid Brezhnev">Leonid Brezhnev</a> became the leader. The era of the 1970s and the early 1980s was later designated as the <a href="/wiki/Era_of_Stagnation" title="Era of Stagnation">Era of Stagnation</a>, a period when economic growth slowed and social policies became static. The 1965 <a href="/wiki/Kosygin_reform" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosygin reform">Kosygin reform</a> aimed for partial <a href="/wiki/Decentralisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Decentralisation">decentralisation</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet economy">Soviet economy</a> and shifted the emphasis from <a href="/wiki/Heavy_industry" title="Heavy industry">heavy industry</a> and weapons to <a href="/wiki/Light_industry" title="Light industry">light industry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Consumer_goods" class="mw-redirect" title="Consumer goods">consumer goods</a> but was stifled by the conservative Communist leadership. In 1979, after a Communist-led revolution in Afghanistan, <a href="/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Afghanistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet invasion of Afghanistan">Soviet forces invaded</a> the country. The occupation drained economic resources and dragged on without achieving meaningful political results. Ultimately, the Soviet Army was withdrawn from Afghanistan in 1989 due to international opposition, persistent anti-Soviet guerrilla warfare, and a lack of support by Soviet citizens. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:President_Reagan_meeting_with_Soviet_General_Secretary_Gorbachev_at_Hofdi_House_during_the_Reykjavik_Summit_Iceland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/President_Reagan_meeting_with_Soviet_General_Secretary_Gorbachev_at_Hofdi_House_during_the_Reykjavik_Summit_Iceland.jpg/220px-President_Reagan_meeting_with_Soviet_General_Secretary_Gorbachev_at_Hofdi_House_during_the_Reykjavik_Summit_Iceland.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/President_Reagan_meeting_with_Soviet_General_Secretary_Gorbachev_at_Hofdi_House_during_the_Reykjavik_Summit_Iceland.jpg/330px-President_Reagan_meeting_with_Soviet_General_Secretary_Gorbachev_at_Hofdi_House_during_the_Reykjavik_Summit_Iceland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/President_Reagan_meeting_with_Soviet_General_Secretary_Gorbachev_at_Hofdi_House_during_the_Reykjavik_Summit_Iceland.jpg/440px-President_Reagan_meeting_with_Soviet_General_Secretary_Gorbachev_at_Hofdi_House_during_the_Reykjavik_Summit_Iceland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2655"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:President_Reagan_meeting_with_Soviet_General_Secretary_Gorbachev_at_Hofdi_House_during_the_Reykjavik_Summit_Iceland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a> in one-to-one discussions with US President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>From 1985 onwards, the last Soviet leader <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a>, who sought to enact liberal reforms in the Soviet system, introduced the policies of <i><a href="/wiki/Glasnost" title="Glasnost">glasnost</a></i> (openness) and <i><a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">perestroika</a></i> (restructuring) in an attempt to end the <a href="/wiki/Era_of_Stagnation" title="Era of Stagnation">period of economic stagnation</a> and to <a href="/wiki/Demokratizatsiya_(Soviet_Union)" title="Demokratizatsiya (Soviet Union)">democratise the government</a>. This, however, led to the rise of strong nationalist and separatist movements. Prior to 1991, the Soviet economy was the world's second-largest,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[84]</a></sup> but during its final years, it was afflicted by shortages of goods in grocery stores, huge budget deficits, and explosive growth in the money supply leading to inflation.<sup id="cite_ref-photius.com_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-photius.com-88">[85]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By 1991, economic and political turmoil began to boil over as the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a> chose to secede from the Soviet Union. On 17 March, a <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_Union_referendum" title="1991 Soviet Union referendum">referendum</a> was held, in which the vast majority of participating citizens voted in favour of changing the Soviet Union into a <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Sovereign_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Union of Sovereign States">renewed federation</a>. In August 1991, <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d'Ã©tat attempt">a coup d'Ã©tat attempt</a> by members of Gorbachev's government, directed against Gorbachev and aimed at preserving the Soviet Union, instead led to the end of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union. On 25 December 1991, the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">Soviet Union dissolved</a>, and along with Russia, fourteen other <a href="/wiki/Post-Soviet_states" title="Post-Soviet states">post-Soviet states</a> emerged. </p> 
      <h3><span id="Post-Soviet_Russia_.281991.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Soviet_Russia_(1991âpresent)">Post-Soviet Russia (1991âpresent)</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Russia_(1991%E2%80%93present)" title="History of Russia (1991âpresent)">History of Russia (1991âpresent)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia_and_the_United_Nations" title="Russia and the United Nations">Russia and the United Nations</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1993_Constitution_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="1993 Constitution of Russia">1993 Constitution of Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a>, <a href="/wiki/War_of_Laws" title="War of Laws">War of Laws</a>, and <a href="/wiki/1993_Russian_constitutional_crisis" title="1993 Russian constitutional crisis">1993 Russian constitutional crisis</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_taking_the_Presidential_Oath,_7_May_2000.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Vladimir_Putin_taking_the_Presidential_Oath%2C_7_May_2000.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_taking_the_Presidential_Oath%2C_7_May_2000.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Vladimir_Putin_taking_the_Presidential_Oath%2C_7_May_2000.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_taking_the_Presidential_Oath%2C_7_May_2000.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Vladimir_Putin_taking_the_Presidential_Oath%2C_7_May_2000.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_taking_the_Presidential_Oath%2C_7_May_2000.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_taking_the_Presidential_Oath,_7_May_2000.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> takes the oath of office as president on his <a href="/wiki/First_inauguration_of_Vladimir_Putin" title="First inauguration of Vladimir Putin">first inauguration</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Boris_Yeltsin" title="Boris Yeltsin">Boris Yeltsin</a> looking over, 2000.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In June 1991, <a href="/wiki/Boris_Yeltsin" title="Boris Yeltsin">Boris Yeltsin</a> became the first directly elected president in Russian history when he was elected President of the Russian SFSR, which became the independent Russian Federation in December of that year. The economic and political collapse of the Soviet Union led to a deep and prolonged depression, characterised by a 50% decline in both GDP and industrial output between 1990 and 1995, although some of the recorded declines may have been a result of an upward bias in Soviet-era economic data.<sup id="cite_ref-OECD_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-89">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[87]</a></sup> During and after the disintegration of the Soviet Union, wide-ranging reforms including <a href="/wiki/Privatization_in_Russia" title="Privatization in Russia">privatisation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">market and trade liberalisation</a> were undertaken,<sup id="cite_ref-OECD_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OECD-89">[86]</a></sup> including radical changes along the lines of "<a href="/wiki/Shock_therapy_(economics)" title="Shock therapy (economics)">shock therapy</a>" as recommended by the United States and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sciolino,_E_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sciolino,_E-91">[88]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The privatisation largely shifted control of enterprises from state agencies to individuals with inside connections in the government. Many of the newly rich moved billions in cash and assets outside of the country in an enormous <a href="/wiki/Capital_flight" title="Capital flight">capital flight</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[89]</a></sup> The depression of the economy led to the collapse of social services; the <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a> plummeted while the <a href="/wiki/Death_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Death rate">death rate</a> skyrocketed.<sup id="cite_ref-TBTCTES106_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TBTCTES106-93">[90]</a></sup> Millions plunged into poverty, from a level of 1.5% in the late Soviet era to 39â49% by mid-1993.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbank_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbank-94">[91]</a></sup> The 1990s saw extreme corruption and lawlessness, the rise of criminal gangs and violent crime.<sup id="cite_ref-Jason_Bush_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jason_Bush-95">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In late 1993, tensions between Yeltsin and the Russian parliament culminated in a <a href="/wiki/1993_Russian_constitutional_crisis" title="1993 Russian constitutional crisis">constitutional crisis</a> which ended after military force. During the crisis, Yeltsin was backed by Western governments, and over 100 people were killed. In December, a <a href="/wiki/1993_Russian_constitutional_referendum" title="1993 Russian constitutional referendum">referendum</a> was held and approved, which introduced a new constitution, giving the president enormous powers. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Obama_and_Medvedev_sign_Prague_Treaty_2010.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Obama_and_Medvedev_sign_Prague_Treaty_2010.jpeg/220px-Obama_and_Medvedev_sign_Prague_Treaty_2010.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Obama_and_Medvedev_sign_Prague_Treaty_2010.jpeg/330px-Obama_and_Medvedev_sign_Prague_Treaty_2010.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Obama_and_Medvedev_sign_Prague_Treaty_2010.jpeg/440px-Obama_and_Medvedev_sign_Prague_Treaty_2010.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="650" data-file-height="434"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Obama_and_Medvedev_sign_Prague_Treaty_2010.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> after signing the <a href="/wiki/New_START" title="New START">New START</a> <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_disarmament" title="Nuclear disarmament">nuclear reduction</a> treaty
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The 1990s were plagued by armed conflicts in the <a href="/wiki/North_Caucasus" title="North Caucasus">North Caucasus</a>, both local ethnic skirmishes and separatist <a href="/wiki/Islamist" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamist">Islamist</a> insurrections. From the time <a href="/wiki/Chechnya" title="Chechnya">Chechen</a> separatists declared independence in the early 1990s, an <a href="/wiki/First_Chechen_War" title="First Chechen War">intermittent guerrilla war</a> has been fought between the rebel groups and the Russian Armed Forces. <a href="/wiki/Terrorism_in_Russia" title="Terrorism in Russia">Terrorist attacks against civilians</a> carried out by separatists, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_theater_hostage_crisis" title="Moscow theater hostage crisis">Moscow theater hostage crisis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beslan_school_siege" title="Beslan school siege">Beslan school siege</a>, caused hundreds of deaths. </p>
      <p>Russia took up the responsibility for settling the Soviet Union's external debts, even though its population made up just half of it at the time of its dissolution.<sup id="cite_ref-Jason_Bush_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jason_Bush-95">[92]</a></sup> In 1992, most consumer price controls were eliminated, causing extreme inflation and significantly devaluing the Ruble.<sup id="cite_ref-Lipton_1992_213_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lipton_1992_213-96">[93]</a></sup> With a devalued ruble, the Russian government struggled to pay back its debts to internal debtors, as well as international institutions like the International Monetary Fund.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[94]</a></sup> Despite significant attempts at economic restructuring, Russia's debt outpaced GDP growth. High budget deficits coupled with increasing capital flight and inability to pay back debts,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[95]</a></sup> caused the 1998 Russian financial crisis,<sup id="cite_ref-Lipton_1992_213_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lipton_1992_213-96">[93]</a></sup> and resulted in a further GDP decline.<sup id="cite_ref-photius.com_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-photius.com-88">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Putin_era">Putin era</span></h4> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Russia_under_Vladimir_Putin" title="Russia under Vladimir Putin">Russia under Vladimir Putin</a>
      </div> 
      <p>On 31 December 1999, President Yeltsin unexpectedly resigned, handing the post to the recently appointed Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>. Yeltsin left office widely unpopular, with an approval rating as low as 2% by some estimates.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[96]</a></sup> Putin then won <a href="/wiki/2000_Russian_presidential_election" title="2000 Russian presidential election">the 2000 presidential election</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Chechen_War" title="Second Chechen War">suppressed the Chechen insurgency</a>. As a result of <a href="/wiki/Price_of_petroleum" class="mw-redirect" title="Price of petroleum">high oil prices</a>, a rise in foreign investment, and prudent economic and fiscal policies, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian economy">Russian economy</a> grew for eight straight years; improving the standard of living, and increasing Russia's influence on the world stage.<sup id="cite_ref-challenges_p12_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-challenges_p12-100">[97]</a></sup> Putin went on to win a <a href="/wiki/2004_Russian_presidential_election" title="2004 Russian presidential election">second presidential term</a> in 2004. Following the <a href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%932008" title="Financial crisis of 2007â2008">global economic crisis of 2008</a> and a subsequent drop in oil prices, Russia's economy stagnated in 2009. And from 2010 to 2013, Russia enjoyed high economic growth; until <a href="/wiki/World_oil_market_chronology_from_2003" title="World oil market chronology from 2003">falling oil prices</a> coupled with <a href="/wiki/International_sanctions_during_the_Ukrainian_crisis" title="International sanctions during the Ukrainian crisis">international sanctions</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexation of Crimea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War" title="Russo-Ukrainian War">Russo-Ukrainian War</a> led to the economy shrinking in 2015, though it rebounded in 2016, and the recession officially ended.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[98]</a></sup> Many reforms made during the Putin presidency have been criticised as authoritarian,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[99]</a></sup> while Putin's leadership over the return of order, stability, and prosperity has won him widespread admiration in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[100]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Putin_with_Vladimir_Konstantinov,_Sergey_Aksyonov_and_Alexey_Chaly_4.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Putin_with_Vladimir_Konstantinov%2C_Sergey_Aksyonov_and_Alexey_Chaly_4.jpeg/220px-Putin_with_Vladimir_Konstantinov%2C_Sergey_Aksyonov_and_Alexey_Chaly_4.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Putin_with_Vladimir_Konstantinov%2C_Sergey_Aksyonov_and_Alexey_Chaly_4.jpeg/330px-Putin_with_Vladimir_Konstantinov%2C_Sergey_Aksyonov_and_Alexey_Chaly_4.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Putin_with_Vladimir_Konstantinov%2C_Sergey_Aksyonov_and_Alexey_Chaly_4.jpeg/440px-Putin_with_Vladimir_Konstantinov%2C_Sergey_Aksyonov_and_Alexey_Chaly_4.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="4091" data-file-height="2722"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Putin_with_Vladimir_Konstantinov,_Sergey_Aksyonov_and_Alexey_Chaly_4.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> (third, left), <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Aksyonov" title="Sergey Aksyonov">Sergey Aksyonov</a> (first, left), <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Konstantinov_(politician)" title="Vladimir Konstantinov (politician)">Vladimir Konstantinov</a> (second, left) and <a href="/wiki/Aleksei_Chalyi" class="mw-redirect" title="Aleksei Chalyi">Aleksei Chalyi</a> (right) sign the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_Accession_of_the_Republic_of_Crimea_to_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty on Accession of the Republic of Crimea to Russia">Treaty on Accession of the Republic of Crimea to Russia</a> in 2014
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On 2 March 2008, <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a> was elected President of Russia while Putin became Prime Minister. The constitution prohibited Putin from serving a third consecutive presidential term. Putin returned to the presidency following the <a href="/wiki/2012_Russian_presidential_election" title="2012 Russian presidential election">2012 presidential elections</a>, and Medvedev was appointed Prime Minister. This quick succession in leadership change was coined "<a href="/wiki/Tandemocracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Tandemocracy">tandemocracy</a>" by outside media. Some critics claimed that the leadership change was superficial, and that Putin remained as the decision making force in the Russian government, while other political analysts viewed it as truly tandem.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[102]</a></sup> Alleged fraud in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Russian_legislative_elections" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Russian legislative elections">2011 parliamentary elections</a> and Putin's return to the presidency in 2012 sparked <a href="/wiki/2011-2013_Russian_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2011-2013 Russian protests">mass protests</a>, which lasted until 2013. </p>
      <p>In 2014, after President <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">Viktor Yanukovych</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> fled as a result of a <a href="/wiki/2014_Ukrainian_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 Ukrainian revolution">revolution</a>, Putin requested and received authorisation from the Russian parliament to <a href="/wiki/2014_Russian_military_intervention_in_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 Russian military intervention in Ukraine">deploy Russian troops to Ukraine</a>, leading to the takeover of Crimea.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[103]</a></sup> Following a <a href="/wiki/2014_Crimean_status_referendum" title="2014 Crimean status referendum">Crimean referendum</a> in which separation was favoured by a large majority of voters,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[104]</a></sup> the Russian leadership announced the accession of Crimea into the Russian Federation, though this and the referendum that preceded it were <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Crimea" title="Political status of Crimea">not accepted internationally</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[105]</a></sup> The annexation of Crimea led to sanctions by Western countries, in which the Russian government responded with its own against a number of countries.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[107]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In September 2015, Russia started <a href="/wiki/Russian_military_intervention_in_the_Syrian_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian military intervention in the Syrian Civil War">military intervention</a> in the Syrian Civil War in support of the Syrian government, consisting of airstrikes against militant groups of the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Nusra_Front" title="Al-Nusra Front">al-Nusra Front</a> (al-Qaeda in the Levant), the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Conquest" title="Army of Conquest">Army of Conquest</a> and other rebel groups. During March 2017 and October 2018, the country saw <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%932018_Russian_protests" title="2017â2018 Russian protests">mass protests</a>, which were primarily concerned with suppressing <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corruption</a> in the Russian government and abandoning the planned retirement age hike. Amidst of the protests, during March 2018, Putin was elected for a <a href="/wiki/2018_Russian_presidential_election" title="2018 Russian presidential election">fourth presidential term</a> overall. </p>
      <p>During July to September 2019, <a href="/wiki/2019_Moscow_protests" title="2019 Moscow protests">protests were held in Moscow</a>, which was caused by the rejection to allow the independent candidates to participate in the <a href="/wiki/2019_Moscow_City_Duma_election" title="2019 Moscow City Duma election">2019 Moscow City Duma election</a>. In January 2020, substantial <a href="/wiki/2020_amendments_to_the_Constitution_of_Russia" title="2020 amendments to the Constitution of Russia">amendments</a> to the constitution were proposed and took effect in July following a <a href="/wiki/2020_Russian_constitutional_referendum" title="2020 Russian constitutional referendum">national vote</a>, allowing Putin to run for two more six-year presidential terms after his current term ends.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[108]</a></sup> In April 2021, Putin signed the constitutional change into law.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[109]</a></sup> Since July 2020, <a href="/wiki/2020%E2%80%932021_Khabarovsk_Krai_protests" title="2020â2021 Khabarovsk Krai protests">protests have been continuing</a> in <a href="/wiki/Khabarovsk_Krai" title="Khabarovsk Krai">Khabarovsk Krai</a> and other regions of Siberia, which was caused by the arrest of <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Furgal" title="Sergei Furgal">Sergei Furgal</a>. In January 2021, <a href="/wiki/2021_Russian_protests" title="2021 Russian protests">widespread protests began</a> across the country, due to the arrest of opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Alexei_Navalny" title="Alexei Navalny">Alexei Navalny</a>, and have been ongoing. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Russia" title="Politics of Russia">Politics of Russia</a>
      </div>

        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a><br><small><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Standard_of_the_President_of_the_Russian_Federation.svg/15px-Standard_of_the_President_of_the_Russian_Federation.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Standard_of_the_President_of_the_Russian_Federation.svg/23px-Standard_of_the_President_of_the_Russian_Federation.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Standard_of_the_President_of_the_Russian_Federation.svg/30px-Standard_of_the_President_of_the_Russian_Federation.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1200"></span> <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="President of the Russian Federation">President</a></small> </td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Mishustin" title="Mikhail Mishustin">Mikhail Mishustin</a><br><small><a href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Russian_Federation_2.svg" class="image"><img alt="Coat of Arms of the Russian Federation 2.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Russian_Federation_2.svg/14px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Russian_Federation_2.svg.png" decoding="async" width="14" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Russian_Federation_2.svg/21px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Russian_Federation_2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Russian_Federation_2.svg/27px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Russian_Federation_2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="355" data-file-height="390"></a> <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of the Russian Federation">Prime Minister</a></small> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Russia" title="Constitution of Russia">Constitution of Russia</a>, the country is an <a href="/wiki/Asymmetric_federalism" title="Asymmetric federalism">asymmetric federation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi-presidential">semi-presidential</a> republic, wherein the President is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[110]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Russia" title="Prime Minister of Russia">Prime Minister</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. The Russian Federation is fundamentally structured as a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a>, with the federal government composed of three branches:<sup id="cite_ref-DeRouenHeo2005_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeRouenHeo2005-114">[111]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Legislative: The <a href="/wiki/Bicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Federal_Assembly_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Assembly of Russia">Federal Assembly of Russia</a>, made up of the 450-member <a href="/wiki/State_Duma" title="State Duma">State Duma</a> and the 170-member <a href="/wiki/Federation_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Federation Council">Federation Council</a>, adopts <a href="/wiki/Federal_law" title="Federal law">federal law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Declaration_of_war" title="Declaration of war">declares war</a>, approves treaties, has the <a href="/wiki/Power_of_the_purse" title="Power of the purse">power of the purse</a> and the power of <a href="/wiki/Impeachment" title="Impeachment">impeachment</a> of the President.</li> 
       <li>Executive: The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Russia" title="President of Russia">President</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Commander-in-Chief_of_the_Armed_Forces_of_the_Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Commander-in-Chief of the Armed Forces of the Russian Federation">Commander-in-Chief</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Armed_Forces" title="Russian Armed Forces">Armed Forces</a>, can veto <a href="/wiki/Legislative_bill" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative bill">legislative bills</a> before they become law, and appoints the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Russia" title="Government of Russia">Government of Russia</a> (Cabinet) and other officers, who administer and enforce federal laws and policies.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Russia" title="Judiciary of Russia">Judiciary</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_Court_of_Russia" title="Constitutional Court of Russia">Constitutional Court</a>, <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Russia" title="Supreme Court of Russia">Supreme Court</a> and lower federal courts, whose judges are appointed by the Federation Council on the recommendation of the President, interpret laws and can overturn laws they deem <a href="/wiki/Unconstitutional" class="mw-redirect" title="Unconstitutional">unconstitutional</a>.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>The president is elected by popular vote for a six-year term (eligible for a second term, but not for a third consecutive term).<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[112]</a></sup> Ministries of the government are composed of the Premier and his deputies, ministers, and selected other individuals; all are appointed by the President on the recommendation of the Prime Minister (whereas the appointment of the latter requires the consent of the State Duma). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_divisions">Political divisions</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Subdivisions of Russia">Subdivisions of Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Crimea_and_Sevastopol" class="mw-redirect" title="Political status of Crimea and Sevastopol">Political status of Crimea and Sevastopol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="center">
       <div class="floatnone">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_(2014).svg" class="image"><img alt="Map of federal subjects of Russia (2014).svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg/690px-Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="690" height="380" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg/1035px-Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg/1380px-Map_of_federal_subjects_of_Russia_%282014%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="282"></a>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Russia" title="Constitution of Russia">constitution</a>, Russia comprises 85 <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia" title="Federal subjects of Russia">federal subjects</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[d]</a></sup> In 1993, when the new constitution was adopted, there were 89 federal subjects listed, but later some of them were merged. These subjects have equal representationâtwo delegates eachâin the <a href="/wiki/Federation_Council_(Russia)" title="Federation Council (Russia)">Federation Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[113]</a></sup> However, they differ in the degree of autonomy they enjoy. </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>46 <a href="/wiki/Oblasts_of_Russia" title="Oblasts of Russia">oblasts</a> (provinces): most common type of federal subjects, with locally elected governor and legislature.<sup id="cite_ref-FZ_gub_elect_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FZ_gub_elect-118">[114]</a></sup></li> 
       <li>22 <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_Russia" title="Republics of Russia">republics</a>: nominally autonomous; each is tasked with drafting its own constitution, direct-elected,<sup id="cite_ref-FZ_gub_elect_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FZ_gub_elect-118">[114]</a></sup> head of republic,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[115]</a></sup> or a similar post, and parliament. Republics are allowed to establish their own official language alongside Russian but are represented by the federal government in international affairs. Republics are meant to be home to specific ethnic minorities.</li> 
       <li>9 <a href="/wiki/Krais_of_Russia" title="Krais of Russia">krais</a> (territories): essentially the same as oblasts. The "territory" designation is historic, originally given to frontier regions and later also to the administrative divisions that comprised autonomous okrugs or autonomous oblasts.</li> 
       <li>4 <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_okrugs_of_Russia" title="Autonomous okrugs of Russia">autonomous okrugs</a> (autonomous districts): originally autonomous entities within oblasts and krais created for ethnic minorities, their status was elevated to that of federal subjects in the 1990s. With the exception of <a href="/wiki/Chukotka_Autonomous_Okrug" title="Chukotka Autonomous Okrug">Chukotka Autonomous Okrug</a>, all autonomous okrugs are still administratively subordinated to a krai or an oblast of which they are a part.</li> 
       <li>1 <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_oblasts_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous oblasts of Russia">autonomous oblast</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Autonomous_Oblast" title="Jewish Autonomous Oblast">Jewish Autonomous Oblast</a>): historically, autonomous oblasts were administrative units subordinated to krais. In 1990, all of them except for the Jewish Autonomous Oblast were elevated in status to that of a republic.</li> 
       <li>3 <a href="/wiki/Federal_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal cities">federal cities</a> (Moscow, Saint Petersburg, and <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a>): major cities that function as separate regions.</li>
      </ul> 
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Federal districts
       </dt>
      </dl> 
      <p>Federal subjects are grouped into eight <a href="/wiki/Federal_districts_of_Russia" title="Federal districts of Russia">federal districts</a>, each administered by an envoy appointed by the President of Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[116]</a></sup> Unlike the federal subjects, the federal districts are not a subnational level of government but are a level of administration of the federal government. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Russia" title="Foreign relations of Russia">Foreign relations of Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Family_photo_of_the_2019_G20_Osaka_summit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Family_photo_of_the_2019_G20_Osaka_summit.jpg/220px-Family_photo_of_the_2019_G20_Osaka_summit.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Family_photo_of_the_2019_G20_Osaka_summit.jpg/330px-Family_photo_of_the_2019_G20_Osaka_summit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Family_photo_of_the_2019_G20_Osaka_summit.jpg/440px-Family_photo_of_the_2019_G20_Osaka_summit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3506" data-file-height="2337"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Family_photo_of_the_2019_G20_Osaka_summit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Putin with G20 counterparts in <a href="/wiki/Osaka" title="Osaka">Osaka</a>, 2019.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Russia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Russia has the fifth-largest diplomatic network in the world; maintaining diplomatic relations with 190 <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations" title="Member states of the United Nations">United Nations member states</a>, two <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">partially-recognized states</a>, and three <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations#Observers_and_non-members" title="Member states of the United Nations">United Nations observer states</a>; with <a href="/wiki/Russian_embassies" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian embassies">144 embassies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[117]</a></sup> It is considered a <a href="/wiki/Potential_superpower" class="mw-redirect" title="Potential superpower">potential superpower</a>; and is one of <a href="/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council" title="Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council">five permanent members</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>. Russia is a member of the <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific_Economic_Cooperation" title="Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation">APEC</a>, and takes a leading role in organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_Economic_Union" title="Eurasian Economic Union">EAEU</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Collective_Security_Treaty_Organisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Collective Security Treaty Organisation">CSTO</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organisation">SCO</a>, and <a href="/wiki/BRICS" title="BRICS">BRICS</a>. </p>
      <p>Russia maintains positive relations with other countries of SCO,<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[118]</a></sup> EAEU,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[119]</a></sup> and BRICS,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[120]</a></sup> especially <a href="/wiki/Belarus%E2%80%93Russia_relations" title="BelarusâRussia relations">with neighbouring Belarus</a>, which is in the <a href="/wiki/Union_State" title="Union State">Union State</a>, a supranational confederation of the latter with Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[121]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> has been a <a href="/wiki/Russia%E2%80%93Serbia_relations" title="RussiaâSerbia relations">historically close ally</a> of Russia since centuries, as both countries share a strong mutual cultural, ethnic, and religious affinity.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[122]</a></sup> In the 21st century, <a href="/wiki/Sino-Russian_relations_since_1991" title="Sino-Russian relations since 1991">Sino-Russian relations</a> have significantly strengthened bilaterally and economicallyâthe <a href="/wiki/2001_Sino-Russian_Treaty_of_Friendship" title="2001 Sino-Russian Treaty of Friendship">Treaty of Friendship</a>, and the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Siberia%E2%80%93Pacific_Ocean_oil_pipeline" title="Eastern SiberiaâPacific Ocean oil pipeline">ESPO oil pipeline</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Power_of_Siberia" title="Power of Siberia">Power of Siberia gas pipeline</a> formed a special relationship between the two.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[123]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> is the largest customer of Russian military equipment, and the two countries share a historically strong <a href="/wiki/India%E2%80%93Russia_relations" title="IndiaâRussia relations">strategic and diplomatic relationship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[124]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Russian_Armed_Forces" title="Russian Armed Forces">Russian Armed Forces</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MilitarySportsHoliday2017-02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/MilitarySportsHoliday2017-02.jpg/220px-MilitarySportsHoliday2017-02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/MilitarySportsHoliday2017-02.jpg/330px-MilitarySportsHoliday2017-02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/MilitarySportsHoliday2017-02.jpg/440px-MilitarySportsHoliday2017-02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MilitarySportsHoliday2017-02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Russian_aircraft_carrier_Admiral_Kuznetsov" title="Russian aircraft carrier Admiral Kuznetsov">Admiral Kuznetsov</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Kuznetsov-class_aircraft_carrier" title="Kuznetsov-class aircraft carrier">Kuznetsov-class aircraft carrier</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Flagship" title="Flagship">flagship</a> of the Russian Navy
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Armed_Forces" title="Russian Armed Forces">Russian Armed Forces</a> are divided into the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Ground_Forces" title="Russian Ground Forces">Ground Forces</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Navy" title="Russian Navy">Navy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Aerospace_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Aerospace Force">Aerospace Forces</a>. There are also two independent arms of service: <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Missile_Troops" class="mw-redirect" title="Strategic Missile Troops">Strategic Missile Troops</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Airborne_Troops" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Airborne Troops">Airborne Troops</a>. As of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Russia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the military had almost one million active-duty personnel, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_military_and_paramilitary_personnel" title="List of countries by number of military and paramilitary personnel">fourth-largest</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Studies2019_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Studies2019-129">[125]</a></sup> Additionally, there are over 2.5 million reservists, with the total number of reserve troops possibly being as high as 20 million.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[126]</a></sup> It is mandatory for all male citizens aged 18â27 to be <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">drafted</a> for a year of service in Armed Forces.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-131">[127]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Russia boasts the world's <a href="/wiki/Military#Capability_development" title="Military">second-most powerful military</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[128]</a></sup> and is among the five <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Non-Proliferation_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Non-Proliferation of Nuclear Weapons">recognised</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_nuclear_weapons" title="List of states with nuclear weapons">nuclear-weapons states</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Russia_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Russia and weapons of mass destruction">largest stockpile of nuclear weapons</a> in the world. More than half of the world's 14,000 nuclear weapons are owned by Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[129]</a></sup> The country possesses the second-largest fleet of <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile_submarine" title="Ballistic missile submarine">ballistic missile submarines</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[130]</a></sup> and is one of the only three states operating <a href="/wiki/Strategic_bomber" title="Strategic bomber">strategic bombers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[131]</a></sup> with the world's most powerful ground force,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[132]</a></sup> the second-most powerful air force,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[133]</a></sup> and the third-most powerful navy fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[134]</a></sup> Russia has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditures" title="List of countries by military expenditures">fourth-highest military expenditure</a> in the world, spending $65.1 billion in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[135]</a></sup> It has a large and fully indigenous <a href="/wiki/Defense_industry_of_Russia" title="Defense industry of Russia">arms industry</a>, producing most of its own military equipment. In 2019, Russia was the world's third-biggest exporter of arms, behind only the United States and China.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[136]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights_and_corruption">Human rights and corruption</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Russia" title="Human rights in Russia">Human rights in Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Russia" title="Corruption in Russia">Corruption in Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Russia's <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Russia" title="Human rights in Russia">human rights</a> management has been increasingly criticised by leading democracy and human rights <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/watchdog" class="extiw" title="wikt:watchdog">watchdogs</a>. In particular, such organisations as <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> consider Russia to have not enough democratic attributes and to allow few political rights and civil liberties to its citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[138]</a></sup> Since 2004, <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> has ranked Russia as "not free" in its <i><a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World" title="Freedom in the World">Freedom in the World</a></i> survey.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[139]</a></sup> Since 2011, the <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a> has ranked Russia as an "authoritarian regime" in its <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a>, ranking it 124th out of 167 countries for 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[140]</a></sup> Russia was ranked 149th out of 180 countries in <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>' <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">Press Freedom Index</a> for 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[141]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Russia was the lowest rated European country in <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Corruption_Perceptions_Index" title="Corruption Perceptions Index">Corruption Perceptions Index</a> for 2020; ranking 129th out of 180 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[142]</a></sup> Corruption is perceived as a significant problem in Russia,<sup id="cite_ref-VOA_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VOA-147">[143]</a></sup> impacting various aspects of life, including the economy,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[144]</a></sup> business,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[145]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Russia" title="Government of Russia">public administration</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Suhara_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suhara-150">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[147]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Russia" title="Law enforcement in Russia">law enforcement</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[148]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Russia" title="Healthcare in Russia">healthcare</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[149]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Russia" title="Education in Russia">education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[150]</a></sup> The phenomenon of corruption is strongly established in the historical model of public governance, and attributed to general weakness of <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a> in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-VOA_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VOA-147">[143]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Russia" title="Geography of Russia">Geography of Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Russland_Relief.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Russland_Relief.png/300px-Russland_Relief.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="192" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Russland_Relief.png/450px-Russland_Relief.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Russland_Relief.png/600px-Russland_Relief.png 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1346"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Russland_Relief.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Topographic_map" title="Topographic map">Topographic map</a> of Russia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Russia is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">largest country</a> in the world, and covers an area of over 17,075,200 square kilometres (6,592,800&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). It is a <a href="/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries" title="List of transcontinental countries">transcontinental country</a>, spanning much of <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>, and stretching vastly over both <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>. Russia has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_length_of_coastline" title="List of countries by length of coastline">fourth-longest coastline</a> in the world, at 37,653&nbsp;km (23,396&nbsp;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[e]</a></sup> and lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/41st_parallel_north" title="41st parallel north">41Â°</a> and <a href="/wiki/82nd_parallel_north" title="82nd parallel north">82Â° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/19th_meridian_east" title="19th meridian east">19Â° E</a> and <a href="/wiki/169th_meridian_west" title="169th meridian west">169Â° W</a>. It is larger, by size, than three <a href="/wiki/Continent" title="Continent">continents</a>: <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>, Europe, and <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a>, and is slightly smaller than the <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_planet" title="Dwarf planet">dwarf planet</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pluto" title="Pluto">Pluto</a> by surface area.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[151]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The two most widely separated points in Russia are about 8,000&nbsp;km (4,971&nbsp;mi) apart along a <a href="/wiki/Geodesic" title="Geodesic">geodesic</a> line.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[f]</a></sup> Mountain ranges are found along the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Russia" title="Southern Russia">southern regions</a>, which shares a part of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus_Mountains" title="Caucasus Mountains">Caucasus Mountains</a> (containing <a href="/wiki/Mount_Elbrus" title="Mount Elbrus">Mount Elbrus</a>; which at 5,642&nbsp;m (18,510&nbsp;ft) is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_elevation_extremes_by_region" title="List of elevation extremes by region">highest</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_ultra-prominent_peaks" title="List of European ultra-prominent peaks">most prominent peak</a> in both Russia and Europe), the <a href="/wiki/Altai_Mountains" title="Altai Mountains">Altai Mountains</a> in <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Verkhoyansk_Range" title="Verkhoyansk Range">Verkhoyansk Range</a> or the volcanoes of <a href="/wiki/Kamchatka_Peninsula" title="Kamchatka Peninsula">Kamchatka Peninsula</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Far_East" title="Russian Far East">Russian Far East</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a>, running north to south through the country's west, are rich in mineral resources, and form the traditional boundary between Europe and Asia. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Volga_river_P8101497_2200_c.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Volga_river_P8101497_2200_c.jpg/220px-Volga_river_P8101497_2200_c.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Volga_river_P8101497_2200_c.jpg/330px-Volga_river_P8101497_2200_c.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Volga_river_P8101497_2200_c.jpg/440px-Volga_river_P8101497_2200_c.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3300" data-file-height="2200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Volga_river_P8101497_2200_c.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Volga" title="Volga">Volga</a>, flowing through <a href="/wiki/Central_Russia" title="Central Russia">Central Russia</a> and into the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">Caspian Sea</a>; is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Europe#Rivers_of_Europe_by_length" title="List of rivers of Europe">longest river</a> in Europe.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Russia, alongside <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, is one of the world's only two countries to have a coast along three <a href="/wiki/Ocean" title="Ocean">oceans</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barents_Sea" title="Barents Sea">Barents Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/White_Sea" title="White Sea">White Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kara_Sea" title="Kara Sea">Kara Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laptev_Sea" title="Laptev Sea">Laptev Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Siberian_Sea" title="East Siberian Sea">East Siberian Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chukchi_Sea" title="Chukchi Sea">Chukchi Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bering_Sea" title="Bering Sea">Bering Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Azov" title="Sea of Azov">Sea of Azov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Okhotsk" title="Sea of Okhotsk">Sea of Okhotsk</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Japan" title="Sea of Japan">Sea of Japan</a> are linked to Russia via the Arctic, Pacific, and the Atlantic. Russia's major islands and archipelagos include <a href="/wiki/Novaya_Zemlya" title="Novaya Zemlya">Novaya Zemlya</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Franz_Josef_Land" title="Franz Josef Land">Franz Josef Land</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Severnaya_Zemlya" title="Severnaya Zemlya">Severnaya Zemlya</a>, the <a href="/wiki/New_Siberian_Islands" title="New Siberian Islands">New Siberian Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wrangel_Island" title="Wrangel Island">Wrangel Island</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands" title="Kuril Islands">Kuril Islands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sakhalin" title="Sakhalin">Sakhalin</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Diomede_Islands" title="Diomede Islands">Diomede Islands</a> are just 3&nbsp;km (1.9&nbsp;mi) apart, and <a href="/wiki/Kunashir_Island" title="Kunashir Island">Kunashir Island</a> is about 20&nbsp;km (12.4&nbsp;mi) from <a href="/wiki/Hokkaido" title="Hokkaido">Hokkaido</a>, Japan. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mount_Elbrus_May_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Mount_Elbrus_May_2008.jpg/220px-Mount_Elbrus_May_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Mount_Elbrus_May_2008.jpg/330px-Mount_Elbrus_May_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Mount_Elbrus_May_2008.jpg/440px-Mount_Elbrus_May_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mount_Elbrus_May_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mount_Elbrus" title="Mount Elbrus">Mount Elbrus</a>, a dormant volcano in <a href="/wiki/Southern_Russia" title="Southern Russia">Southern Russia</a>, is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_elevation_extremes_by_region" title="List of elevation extremes by region">highest mountain</a> in Russia and Europe.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Russia, home to over 100,000 rivers,<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[152]</a></sup> has one of the world's largest surface water resources; with its lakes containing approximately one-quarter of the world's liquid <a href="/wiki/Fresh_water" title="Fresh water">fresh water</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-159">[153]</a></sup> The largest and most prominent of Russia's bodies of fresh water is <a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Lake Baikal</a>, the world's deepest, purest, oldest and most capacious fresh water lake;<sup id="cite_ref-baikal_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-baikal-160">[154]</a></sup> which alone contains over one-fifth of the world's fresh surface water.<sup id="cite_ref-loc_159-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-loc-159">[153]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ladoga" title="Lake Ladoga">Ladoga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Onega" title="Lake Onega">Onega</a> in northern Russia are two of the <a href="/wiki/Largest_lakes" class="mw-redirect" title="Largest lakes">largest lakes</a> in Europe. Russia is second only to <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> in volume of the <a href="/wiki/Total_renewable_water_resources" class="mw-redirect" title="Total renewable water resources">total renewable water resources</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Volga" title="Volga">Volga</a>, widely seen as Russia's national river due to its historical importance,<sup id="cite_ref-rivers_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rivers-161">[155]</a></sup> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Europe#Rivers_of_Europe_by_length" title="List of rivers of Europe">longest river</a> in Europe. The Siberian rivers of <a href="/wiki/Ob_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Ob River">Ob</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yenisey" title="Yenisey">Yenisey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lena_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Lena River">Lena</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amur_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Amur River">Amur</a> are among the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_longest_rivers" class="mw-redirect" title="World's longest rivers">world's longest rivers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rivers_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rivers-161">[155]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Russia" title="Climate of Russia">Climate of Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:300px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Russia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Russia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/298px-Russia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png" decoding="async" width="298" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Russia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/447px-Russia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Russia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg/596px-Russia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="990" data-file-height="792"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Russia_K%C3%B6ppen.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="KÃ¶ppen climate classification">KÃ¶ppen climate classification</a> of Russia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The enormous size of Russia and the remoteness of many areas from the sea result in the dominance of the <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a>, which is prevalent in all parts of the country except for the tundra and the extreme southwest. Mountains in the south obstruct the flow of warm air masses from the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a>, while the plain of the west and north makes the country open to Arctic and Atlantic influences.<sup id="cite_ref-congress_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-congress-162">[156]</a></sup> Most of <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Russia" title="Northwest Russia">Northwest Russia</a> and Siberia has a <a href="/wiki/Subarctic_climate" title="Subarctic climate">subarctic climate</a>, with extremely severe winters in the inner regions of Northeast Siberia (mostly <a href="/wiki/Sakha" title="Sakha">Sakha</a>, where the Northern <a href="/wiki/Pole_of_Cold" title="Pole of Cold">Pole of Cold</a> is located with the record low temperature of â71.2&nbsp;Â°C or â96.2&nbsp;Â°F), and more moderate winters elsewhere. Both the strip of land along the shore of the Arctic Ocean and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Arctic_islands" title="Russian Arctic islands">Russian Arctic islands</a> have a <a href="/wiki/Polar_climate" title="Polar climate">polar climate</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lake_Baikal_in_winter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Lake_Baikal_in_winter.jpg/220px-Lake_Baikal_in_winter.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Lake_Baikal_in_winter.jpg/330px-Lake_Baikal_in_winter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Lake_Baikal_in_winter.jpg/440px-Lake_Baikal_in_winter.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7360" data-file-height="4912"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lake_Baikal_in_winter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Lake_Baikal" title="Lake Baikal">Lake Baikal</a> in winter, near <a href="/wiki/Olkhon_Island" title="Olkhon Island">Olkhon Island</a>. It is the deepest <a href="/wiki/Lake" title="Lake">lake</a> in the world.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The coastal part of <a href="/wiki/Krasnodar_Krai" title="Krasnodar Krai">Krasnodar Krai</a> on the Black Sea, most notably in <a href="/wiki/Sochi" title="Sochi">Sochi</a>, possesses a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> with mild and wet winters. In many regions of East Siberia and the Far East, winter is dry compared to summer; other parts of the country experience more even precipitation across seasons. Winter precipitation in most parts of the country usually falls as snow. The region along the Lower Volga and Caspian Sea coast, as well as some areas of southernmost Siberia, possesses a <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid climate</a>. </p>
      <p>Throughout much of the territory, there are only two distinct seasonsâwinter and summerâas spring and autumn are usually brief periods of change between extremely low and extremely high temperatures.<sup id="cite_ref-congress_162-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-congress-162">[156]</a></sup> The coldest month is January (February on the coastline); the warmest is usually July. Great ranges of temperature are typical. In winter, temperatures get colder both from south to north and from west to east. Summers can be quite hot, even in Siberia.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[157]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_ecoregions_in_Russia" title="List of ecoregions in Russia">List of ecoregions in Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Russia" title="List of mammals of Russia">List of mammals of Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Russia" title="List of birds of Russia">List of birds of Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_freshwater_fish_of_Russia" title="List of freshwater fish of Russia">List of freshwater fish of Russia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Russia" title="Wildlife of Russia">Wildlife of Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>From north to south the <a href="/wiki/East_European_Plain" title="East European Plain">East European Plain</a>, is clad sequentially in Arctic <a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">taiga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mixed_and_broad-leaf_forests" class="mw-redirect" title="Mixed and broad-leaf forests">mixed and broad-leaf forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppe</a>, and semi-desert (fringing the Caspian Sea), as the changes in vegetation reflect the changes in climate. Siberia supports a similar sequence but is largely taiga. About half of Russia's total territory is <a href="/wiki/European_countries_by_forest_area" title="European countries by forest area">forested</a>, and it has the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Forest_reserves" class="mw-redirect" title="Forest reserves">forest reserves</a>, known as the "Lungs of Europe";<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[158]</a></sup> which is second only to the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon rainforest</a> in the amount of <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a> it absorbs. </p>
      <p>There are 266 mammal species and 780 bird species in Russia. A total of 415 animal species were included in the <a href="/wiki/Red_Data_Book_of_the_Russian_Federation" title="Red Data Book of the Russian Federation">RDBRF</a> in 1997; and are now protected.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[159]</a></sup> There are 40 <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/Biosphere_reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Biosphere reserve">biosphere reserves</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[160]</a></sup> 64 <a href="/wiki/National_parks_of_Russia" title="National parks of Russia">national parks</a> and 101 <a href="/wiki/Zapovednik" title="Zapovednik">nature reserves</a>. Russia still has many ecosystems which are still untouched by manâmainly in the northern <a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">taiga</a> areas, and in subarctic tundra of Siberia. Over time Russia has been having improvement and application of <a href="/wiki/Environmental_legislation" class="mw-redirect" title="Environmental legislation">environmental legislation</a>, development and implementation of various federal and regional strategies and programmes, and study, inventory and protection of rare and endangered plants, animals, and other organisms, and including them in the RDBRF.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[161]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Russia" title="Economy of Russia">Economy of Russia</a>
      </div>
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_the_Russian_Federation" title="Economic history of the Russian Federation">Economic history of the Russian Federation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taxation_in_Russia" title="Taxation in Russia">Taxation in Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Business_Centre_of_Moscow_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Business_Centre_of_Moscow_2.jpg/220px-Business_Centre_of_Moscow_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Business_Centre_of_Moscow_2.jpg/330px-Business_Centre_of_Moscow_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Business_Centre_of_Moscow_2.jpg/440px-Business_Centre_of_Moscow_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1333"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Business_Centre_of_Moscow_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Moscow_International_Business_Center" title="Moscow International Business Center">Moscow</a> is a major <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial hub</a> in Europe.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
