        <a href="/wiki/File:HDP_PPP_per_capita_Russia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/HDP_PPP_per_capita_Russia.jpg/220px-HDP_PPP_per_capita_Russia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/HDP_PPP_per_capita_Russia.jpg/330px-HDP_PPP_per_capita_Russia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/HDP_PPP_per_capita_Russia.jpg/440px-HDP_PPP_per_capita_Russia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="961" data-file-height="624"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:HDP_PPP_per_capita_Russia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Russia's GDP growth by purchasing power parity (PPP) during 1991â2019 in <a href="/wiki/International_dollars" class="mw-redirect" title="International dollars">international dollars</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Russia has an upper-middle income <a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transition_economy" title="Transition economy">transition economy</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-https://datahelpdesk.worldbank.org_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-https://datahelpdesk.worldbank.org-168">[162]</a></sup> with enormous natural resources, particularly <a href="/wiki/Russian_oil_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian oil industry">oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_in_Russia" title="Natural gas in Russia">natural gas</a>. It has the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">eleventh-largest economy</a> by nominal GDP and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP)">sixth-largest</a> by <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a>, Russia's GDP per capita by PPP is $29,485 as of 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-IMFWEORU_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMFWEORU-11">[9]</a></sup> The average nominal salary in Russia was â½51,083 per month in 2020,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[163]</a></sup> and 12.9% of Russians lived <a href="/wiki/Poverty_by_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Poverty by country">below the national poverty line</a> in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[164]</a></sup> Approximately 4.5% of Russians were unemployed in 2019,<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[165]</a></sup> and officially more than 70% Russia's population is categorised as middle class;<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[166]</a></sup> which has been disputed by some analysts.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[168]</a></sup> By the end of December 2019, Russian foreign trade turnover reached $666.6 billion. Russia's exports totalled over $422.8 billion, while its imported goods were worth over $243.8 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[169]</a></sup> As of December&nbsp;2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Russia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, foreign reserves in Russia are worth $444 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[170]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Oil, natural gas, metals, and timber account for more than 80% of Russian exports abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-131">[127]</a></sup> In 2016, the oil-and-gas sector accounted for 36% of federal budget revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-EIA_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EIA-177">[171]</a></sup> In 2019, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Natural_Resources_and_Environment_(Russia)" title="Ministry of Natural Resources and Environment (Russia)">Natural Resources and Environment Ministry</a> estimated the value of natural resources to 60% of the country's GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[172]</a></sup> Russia has <a href="/wiki/Foreign_debt_by_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign debt by country">one of the lowest foreign debts among major economies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[173]</a></sup> It ranked 28th of 190 countries in the 2019 <a href="/wiki/Ease_of_doing_business_index" title="Ease of doing business index">Ease of Doing Business Index</a>. Russia has a <a href="/wiki/Flat_tax" title="Flat tax">flat tax</a> rate of 13%; with the world's second-most attractive personal tax system for single managers after the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[174]</a></sup> However, extreme <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_income_equality" title="List of countries by income equality">inequality of household income and wealth</a> in the country has also been noted.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[176]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Russia" title="Transport in Russia">Transport in Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Russia" title="Energy in Russia">Energy in Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Railway transport in Russia is mostly under the control of the state-run <a href="/wiki/Russian_Railways" title="Russian Railways">Russian Railways</a>. The total length of common-used railway tracks exceeds 85,500&nbsp;km (53,127&nbsp;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[177]</a></sup> second only to the United States. The most renowned railway in Russia is the Trans-Siberian Railway, the longest railway-line in the world. As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Russia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Russia has <a href="/wiki/Roads_by_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Roads by country">1,452.2 thousand&nbsp;km of roads</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[178]</a></sup> and its road density is among the lowest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[179]</a></sup> Much of Russia's inland waterways, which <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_waterways_length" title="List of countries by waterways length">total 102,000&nbsp;km (63,380&nbsp;mi)</a>, are made up of natural rivers or lakes. Among Russia's 1,216 airports,<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[180]</a></sup> the busiest are <a href="/wiki/Sheremetyevo" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheremetyevo">Sheremetyevo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domodedovo_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Domodedovo International Airport">Domodedovo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vnukovo_International_Airport" title="Vnukovo International Airport">Vnukovo</a> in Moscow, and <a href="/wiki/Pulkovo_Airport" title="Pulkovo Airport">Pulkovo</a> in Saint Petersburg. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:VL_85-022_container_train.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/VL_85-022_container_train.jpg/220px-VL_85-022_container_train.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/VL_85-022_container_train.jpg/330px-VL_85-022_container_train.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/VL_85-022_container_train.jpg/440px-VL_85-022_container_train.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1154" data-file-height="825"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:VL_85-022_container_train.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_Railway" title="Trans-Siberian Railway">Trans-Siberian Railway</a> is the longest railway line in the world, connecting Moscow to <a href="/wiki/Vladivostok" title="Vladivostok">Vladivostok</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Major seaports of Russia include <a href="/wiki/Rostov-on-Don" title="Rostov-on-Don">Rostov-on-Don</a> on the Sea of Azov, <a href="/wiki/Novorossiysk" title="Novorossiysk">Novorossiysk</a> on the Black Sea, <a href="/wiki/Astrakhan" title="Astrakhan">Astrakhan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Makhachkala" title="Makhachkala">Makhachkala</a> on the Caspian Sea, <a href="/wiki/Kaliningrad" title="Kaliningrad">Kaliningrad</a> and Saint Petersburg on the Baltic Sea, <a href="/wiki/Arkhangelsk" title="Arkhangelsk">Arkhangelsk</a> on the White Sea, <a href="/wiki/Murmansk" title="Murmansk">Murmansk</a> on the Barents Sea, <a href="/wiki/Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky" title="Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky">Petropavlovsk-Kamchatsky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vladivostok" title="Vladivostok">Vladivostok</a> on the Pacific Ocean. Russia is the world's sole country to operate <a href="/wiki/Nuclear-powered_icebreaker" title="Nuclear-powered icebreaker">nuclear-powered icebreakers</a>, which advance the economic exploitation of the Arctic <a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf_of_Russia" title="Continental shelf of Russia">continental shelf of Russia</a>, and the development of sea trade through the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Sea_Route" title="Northern Sea Route">Northern Sea Route</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[181]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:RF_NG_pipestoEU.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/RF_NG_pipestoEU.gif/220px-RF_NG_pipestoEU.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/RF_NG_pipestoEU.gif/330px-RF_NG_pipestoEU.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/RF_NG_pipestoEU.gif/440px-RF_NG_pipestoEU.gif 2x" data-file-width="590" data-file-height="757"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:RF_NG_pipestoEU.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Russia is a major <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">gas</a> supplier to the rest of Europe.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Russia is described as an <a href="/wiki/Energy_superpower" title="Energy superpower">energy superpower</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[182]</a></sup> with the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_reserves" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural gas reserves">natural gas reserves</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[183]</a></sup> the second-largest <a href="/wiki/Coal_reserves" class="mw-redirect" title="Coal reserves">coal reserves</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[184]</a></sup> the eighth-largest <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves" title="Oil reserves">oil reserves</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[185]</a></sup> and the largest <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale_reserves" title="Oil shale reserves">oil shale reserves</a> in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[186]</a></sup> It is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_exports" title="List of countries by natural gas exports">leading natural gas exporter</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[187]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_production" title="List of countries by natural gas production">second-largest natural gas producer</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cia-gas_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-gas-194">[188]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_oil_exports" title="List of countries by oil exports">second-largest oil exporter</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[189]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_oil_production" title="List of countries by oil production">third-largest oil producer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[190]</a></sup> Fossil fuels cause most of the <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions_by_Russia" title="Greenhouse gas emissions by Russia">greenhouse gas emissions by Russia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[191]</a></sup> The country is the world's fourth-largest <a href="/wiki/Electricity_producer" class="mw-redirect" title="Electricity producer">electricity producer</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[192]</a></sup> and the ninth-largest <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy_producer" class="mw-redirect" title="Renewable energy producer">renewable energy producer</a> in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[193]</a></sup> Russia was also the world's first country to develop civilian nuclear power, and to construct the <a href="/wiki/Obninsk_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Obninsk Nuclear Power Plant">first nuclear power plant</a>. In 2019, It was the world's fourth-largest <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_by_country" title="Nuclear power by country">nuclear energy producer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[194]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture_and_fishery">Agriculture and fishery</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Russia" title="Agriculture in Russia">Agriculture in Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fishing_industry_in_Russia" title="Fishing industry in Russia">Fishing industry in Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Russia has the <a href="/wiki/Land_use_statistics_by_country" title="Land use statistics by country">fourth-largest cultivated area</a> in the world, at 1,237,294 square kilometres (477,722&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi); possessing 7.4% of the world's total <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arable land</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[195]</a></sup> It is the third-largest grain exporter;<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[196]</a></sup> and is the top producer of <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buckwheat" title="Buckwheat">buckwheat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oats" class="mw-redirect" title="Oats">oats</a>, and one of the largest producers and exporters of <a href="/wiki/Rye" title="Rye">rye</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sunflower_seed" title="Sunflower seed">sunflower seed</a>. Since 2016, Russia is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_wheat_exports" title="List of countries by wheat exports">largest exporter of wheat</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[197]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>While large farms concentrate mainly on grain production and <a href="/wiki/Animal_husbandry" title="Animal husbandry">animal husbandry</a>, while small private <a href="/wiki/Household_plot" title="Household plot">household plots</a> produce most of the country's potatoes, vegetables and fruits.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[198]</a></sup> Russia is the home to the finest <a href="/wiki/Caviar" title="Caviar">caviar</a> in the world;<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[199]</a></sup> and maintains one of the <a href="/wiki/Fishing_industry_by_country" title="Fishing industry by country">world's largest fishing fleets</a>, ranking sixth in the world in tonnage of fish caught; capturing 4,773,413 tons of fish in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[200]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Russian_inventions_and_technology_records" class="mw-redirect" title="Timeline of Russian inventions and technology records">Timeline of Russian inventions and technology records</a>, <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Russia" title="Science and technology in Russia">Science and technology in Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Russian_scientists" title="List of Russian scientists">List of Russian scientists</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Russian_inventors" title="List of Russian inventors">List of Russian inventors</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:M.V._Lomonosov_by_L.Miropolskiy_after_G.C.Prenner_(1787,_RAN).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/M.V._Lomonosov_by_L.Miropolskiy_after_G.C.Prenner_%281787%2C_RAN%29.jpg/170px-M.V._Lomonosov_by_L.Miropolskiy_after_G.C.Prenner_%281787%2C_RAN%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/M.V._Lomonosov_by_L.Miropolskiy_after_G.C.Prenner_%281787%2C_RAN%29.jpg/255px-M.V._Lomonosov_by_L.Miropolskiy_after_G.C.Prenner_%281787%2C_RAN%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/M.V._Lomonosov_by_L.Miropolskiy_after_G.C.Prenner_%281787%2C_RAN%29.jpg/340px-M.V._Lomonosov_by_L.Miropolskiy_after_G.C.Prenner_%281787%2C_RAN%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="597" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:M.V._Lomonosov_by_L.Miropolskiy_after_G.C.Prenner_(1787,_RAN).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lomonosov" title="Mikhail Lomonosov">Mikhail Lomonosov</a> (1711â1765), <a href="/wiki/Polymath" title="Polymath">polymath</a> scientist, inventor, poet and artist
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Russia's <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> budget is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_research_and_development_spending" title="List of countries by research and development spending">ninth-highest</a> in the world, with an expenditure of approximately 422 billion rubles on domestic research and development.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[201]</a></sup> In 2019, Russia was ranked tenth worldwide in the number of scientific publications.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[202]</a></sup> Since 1904, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_country" title="List of Nobel laureates by country">Nobel Prize</a> were awarded to twenty-six Russian and Soviet people in <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physics" title="Nobel Prize in Physics">physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">chemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_medicine" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prize in medicine">medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Memorial_Prize_in_Economic_Sciences" title="Nobel Memorial Prize in Economic Sciences">economy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">literature</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">peace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[203]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lomonosov" title="Mikhail Lomonosov">Mikhail Lomonosov</a> proposed the law of conservation of matter preceding the <a href="/wiki/Energy_conservation_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy conservation law">energy conservation law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mes_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mes-210">[204]</a></sup> Since the time of <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Lobachevsky" class="mw-redirect" title="Nikolay Lobachevsky">Nikolay Lobachevsky</a> (the "<a href="/wiki/Copernicus" class="mw-redirect" title="Copernicus">Copernicus</a> of <a href="/wiki/Geometry" title="Geometry">Geometry</a>" who pioneered the <a href="/wiki/Non-Euclidean_geometry" title="Non-Euclidean geometry">non-Euclidean geometry</a>) and a prominent tutor <a href="/wiki/Pafnuty_Chebyshev" title="Pafnuty Chebyshev">Pafnuty Chebyshev</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_mathematical_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian mathematical school">Russian mathematical school</a> became one of the most influential in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[205]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Mendeleev" class="mw-redirect" title="Dmitry Mendeleev">Dmitry Mendeleev</a> invented the <a href="/wiki/Periodic_table" title="Periodic table">Periodic table</a>, the main framework of modern <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mes_210-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mes-210">[204]</a></sup> Nine Soviet/Russian mathematicians were awarded with the <a href="/wiki/Fields_Medal" title="Fields Medal">Fields Medal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[206]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Grigori_Perelman" title="Grigori Perelman">Grigori Perelman</a> was offered the first ever Clay <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Prize_Problems" title="Millennium Prize Problems">Millennium Prize Problems</a> Award for his final proof of the <a href="/wiki/Poincar%C3%A9_conjecture" title="PoincarÃ© conjecture">PoincarÃ© conjecture</a> in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[207]</a></sup> Russian discoveries and inventions include the <a href="/wiki/Transformer" title="Transformer">transformer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Incandescent_light_bulb" title="Incandescent light bulb">electric filament lamp</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Aircraft" title="Aircraft">aircraft</a>, the safety <a href="/wiki/Parachute" title="Parachute">parachute</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sputnik_1" title="Sputnik 1">sputnik</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radio_receiver" title="Radio receiver">radio receiver</a>, electrical <a href="/wiki/Microscope" title="Microscope">microscope</a>, <a href="/wiki/Color_photography" title="Color photography">colour photos</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[208]</a></sup> caterpillar tracks, <a href="/wiki/Periodic_table" title="Periodic table">periodic table</a>, track assembly, electrically powered <a href="/wiki/Railroad_car" title="Railroad car">railway wagons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Video_tape_recorder" title="Video tape recorder">videotape recorder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helicopter" title="Helicopter">helicopter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solar_cell" title="Solar cell">solar cell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Transformer" title="Transformer">transformers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yogurt" title="Yogurt">yogurt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">television</a>, petrol <a href="/wiki/Cracking_(chemistry)" title="Cracking (chemistry)">cracking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Synthetic_rubber" title="Synthetic rubber">synthetic rubber</a> and <a href="/wiki/Combine_harvester" title="Combine harvester">grain harvester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[209]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Russia%26_-39;s_Mir_space_station_is_backdropped_against_Earth%26_-39;s_horizon._Original_from_NASA_._Digitally_enhanced_by_rawpixel._-_41997987775.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Russia%26_-39%3Bs_Mir_space_station_is_backdropped_against_Earth%26_-39%3Bs_horizon._Original_from_NASA_._Digitally_enhanced_by_rawpixel._-_41997987775.jpg/220px-Russia%26_-39%3Bs_Mir_space_station_is_backdropped_against_Earth%26_-39%3Bs_horizon._Original_from_NASA_._Digitally_enhanced_by_rawpixel._-_41997987775.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Russia%26_-39%3Bs_Mir_space_station_is_backdropped_against_Earth%26_-39%3Bs_horizon._Original_from_NASA_._Digitally_enhanced_by_rawpixel._-_41997987775.jpg/330px-Russia%26_-39%3Bs_Mir_space_station_is_backdropped_against_Earth%26_-39%3Bs_horizon._Original_from_NASA_._Digitally_enhanced_by_rawpixel._-_41997987775.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Russia%26_-39%3Bs_Mir_space_station_is_backdropped_against_Earth%26_-39%3Bs_horizon._Original_from_NASA_._Digitally_enhanced_by_rawpixel._-_41997987775.jpg/440px-Russia%26_-39%3Bs_Mir_space_station_is_backdropped_against_Earth%26_-39%3Bs_horizon._Original_from_NASA_._Digitally_enhanced_by_rawpixel._-_41997987775.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2334" data-file-height="2500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Russia%26_-39;s_Mir_space_station_is_backdropped_against_Earth%26_-39;s_horizon._Original_from_NASA_._Digitally_enhanced_by_rawpixel._-_41997987775.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a>, Soviet and Russian <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">space station</a> that operated in <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">low Earth orbit</a> from 1986 to 2001.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Roscosmos" title="Roscosmos">Roscosmos</a> is Russia's national space agency; while Russian achievements in the field of <a href="/wiki/Space_technology" title="Space technology">space technology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">space exploration</a> are traced back to <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Tsiolkovsky" title="Konstantin Tsiolkovsky">Konstantin Tsiolkovsky</a>, the father of theoretical <a href="/wiki/Astronautics" title="Astronautics">astronautics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[210]</a></sup> His works had inspired leading Soviet rocket engineers, such as <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Korolyov" class="mw-redirect" title="Sergey Korolyov">Sergey Korolyov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valentin_Glushko" title="Valentin Glushko">Valentin Glushko</a>, and many others who contributed to the success of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_space_program" title="Soviet space program">Soviet space program</a> in the early stages of the <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">Space Race</a> and beyond. </p>
      <p>In 1957, the first Earth-orbiting artificial <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Sputnik_1" title="Sputnik 1">Sputnik&nbsp;1</a></i>, was launched; in 1961 the first human trip into space was successfully made by <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">Yuri Gagarin</a>. Many other Soviet and Russian <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration_records" class="mw-redirect" title="Space exploration records">space exploration records</a> ensued, including the first <a href="/wiki/Spacewalk" class="mw-redirect" title="Spacewalk">spacewalk</a> performed by <a href="/wiki/Alexei_Leonov" title="Alexei Leonov">Alexei Leonov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luna_9" title="Luna 9">Luna&nbsp;9</a> was the first spacecraft to land on the <a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">Moon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zond_5" title="Zond 5">Zond 5</a> brought the first Earthlings (two tortoises and other life forms) to circumnavigate the Moon, <a href="/wiki/Venera_7" title="Venera 7">Venera&nbsp;7</a> was the first to land on another planet (<a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">Venus</a>), <a href="/wiki/Mars_3" title="Mars 3">Mars&nbsp;3</a> then the first to land on <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration_rover" class="mw-redirect" title="Space exploration rover">space exploration rover</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Lunokhod-1" class="mw-redirect" title="Lunokhod-1">Lunokhod 1</a></i>, and the first <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">space station</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Salyut_1" title="Salyut 1">Salyut&nbsp;1</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a></i>. Russia is the largest satellite launcher.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[211]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Russia has completed the <a href="/wiki/GLONASS" title="GLONASS">GLONASS</a> <a href="/wiki/Satellite_navigation_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Satellite navigation system">satellite navigation system</a>, and is developing its own <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi_PAK_FA" class="mw-redirect" title="Sukhoi PAK FA">fifth-generation jet fighter</a> and constructing the first serial <a href="/wiki/Mobile_nuclear_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Mobile nuclear plant">mobile nuclear plant</a> in the world. <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_(rocket_family)" title="Soyuz (rocket family)">Soyuz rockets</a> are the only provider of transport for astronauts at the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>. <a href="/wiki/Luna-Glob" title="Luna-Glob">Luna-Glob</a> is a Russian Moon exploration programme, with first planned mission launch in 2021. Roscosmos is also developing the <a href="/wiki/Orel_spacecraft" class="mw-redirect" title="Orel spacecraft">Orel spacecraft</a>, to replace the aging Soyuz, it could also conduct mission to lunar orbit as early as 2026.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[212]</a></sup> In February 2019, it was announced that Russia is intending to conduct its first crewed mission to land on the Moon in 2031.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[213]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Russia" title="Tourism in Russia">Tourism in Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Grand_Cascade_in_Peterhof_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Grand_Cascade_in_Peterhof_01.jpg/220px-Grand_Cascade_in_Peterhof_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Grand_Cascade_in_Peterhof_01.jpg/330px-Grand_Cascade_in_Peterhof_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Grand_Cascade_in_Peterhof_01.jpg/440px-Grand_Cascade_in_Peterhof_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4200" data-file-height="2800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Grand_Cascade_in_Peterhof_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Peterhof_Palace" title="Peterhof Palace">Peterhof Palace</a> in Saint Petersburg, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Tourism_Organization" title="World Tourism Organization">World Tourism Organization</a>, Russia was the sixteenth-most visited country in the world, and the tenth-most visited country in Europe, in 2018, with over 24.6 million visits.<sup id="cite_ref-unwto_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unwto-220">[214]</a></sup> Russia was ranked 39th in the Travel and Tourism Competitiveness Report 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[215]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Federal_Agency_for_Tourism_(Russia)" title="Federal Agency for Tourism (Russia)">Federal Agency for Tourism</a>, the number of inbound trips of foreign citizens to Russia amounted to 24.4 million in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[216]</a></sup> Russia's international tourism receipts in 2018 amounted to $11.6 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-unwto_220-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unwto-220">[214]</a></sup> In 2020, tourism accounted for about 4% of country's GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[217]</a></sup> Major tourist routes in Russia include a journey around the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Ring_of_Russia" title="Golden Ring of Russia">Golden Ring of Russia</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Theme_route" class="mw-redirect" title="Theme route">theme route</a> of ancient Russian cities, cruises on large rivers like the Volga, and journeys on the famous Trans-Siberian Railway.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[218]</a></sup> Russia's most visited and popular landmarks include <a href="/wiki/Red_Square" title="Red Square">Red Square</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Peterhof_Palace" title="Peterhof Palace">Peterhof Palace</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Kazan_Kremlin" title="Kazan Kremlin">Kazan Kremlin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Lavra_of_St._Sergius" title="Trinity Lavra of St. Sergius">Trinity Lavra of St. Sergius</a> and Lake Baikal.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[219]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Russia" title="Demographics of Russia">Demographics of Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Russia is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population_density" title="List of countries and dependencies by population density">most sparsely populated</a> and <a href="/wiki/Urbanization_by_country" title="Urbanization by country">urbanised</a> countries in the world; it had a population of 142.8 million according to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Census_(2010)" title="Russian Census (2010)">2010 census</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-2010Census_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010Census-226">[220]</a></sup> which rose to 146.2 million as of 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-gks.ru-popul_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gks.ru-popul-10">[8]</a></sup> It is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_countries_by_population" title="List of European countries by population">most populous country</a> in Europe, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population" title="List of countries and dependencies by population">ninth-most populous country</a> in the world; with a <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_density" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by population density">population density</a> of 9 inhabitants per square kilometre (23 per square mile). </p>
      <p>Since the 1990s, Russia's <a href="/wiki/Death_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Death rate">death rate</a> has exceeded its <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[221]</a></sup> In 2018, the <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> across Russia was estimated to be 1.6 children born per woman, which is below the replacement rate of 2.1, and is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependencies_by_total_fertility_rate" title="List of sovereign states and dependencies by total fertility rate">lowest fertility rates in the world</a>. Subsequently, the nation has one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_median_age" title="List of countries by median age">oldest populations in the world</a>, with an median age of 40.3 years.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[222]</a></sup> In 2009, it recorded annual population growth for the first time in fifteen years; and since the 2010s, Russia has seen increased population growth due to declining <a href="/wiki/Death_rates" class="mw-redirect" title="Death rates">death rates</a>, increased <a href="/wiki/Birth_rates" class="mw-redirect" title="Birth rates">birth rates</a> and increased <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigration</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[223]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Russia is a <a href="/wiki/Multinational_state" title="Multinational state">multinational state</a>, home to over 193 ethnic groups nationwide.<sup id="cite_ref-ethnicgroups_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicgroups-230">[224]</a></sup> In the 2010 Census, roughly 81% of the population were ethnic <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ethnicgroups_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ethnicgroups-230">[224]</a></sup> and rest of the 19% of the population were peoples of diverse origins,<sup id="cite_ref-perepis-2010.ru_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perepis-2010.ru-4">[3]</a></sup> while roughly 85% of Russia's population was of <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_of_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Ethnic groups of Europe">European descent</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-perepis-2010.ru_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-perepis-2010.ru-4">[3]</a></sup> of which the vast majority were <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a>, with a substantial minority of <a href="/wiki/Finno-Ugric_peoples" title="Finno-Ugric peoples">Finno-Ugric</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic</a>, and other peoples. There are <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_Russia" title="Republics of Russia">22 republics</a> in Russia, designated to have their own ethnicities, cultures, and languages. In 13 of them, ethnic Russians <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_Russia#Demographics_trend" title="Republics of Russia">consist a minority</a>. According to the United Nations, Russia's <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Russia" title="Immigration to Russia">immigrant population</a> is the third-largest in the world, numbering over 11.6 million;<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[225]</a></sup> most of which are from <a href="/wiki/Post-Soviet_states" title="Post-Soviet states">post-Soviet states</a>, mainly <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians_in_Russia" title="Ukrainians in Russia">Ukrainians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[226]</a></sup> </p>

         <td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">2</td>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="***REMOVED***">Language</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian language</a> and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Russia" title="Languages of Russia">Languages of Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;max-width:352px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="theader">
          Minority languages across Russia
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:121px;max-width:121px">

          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <span style="font-family:sans-serif;font-size:100%;color:black;background-color:transparent;;"><a href="/wiki/Altaic_languages" title="Altaic languages">Altaic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uralic_languages" title="Uralic languages">Uralic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yukaghir_languages" title="Yukaghir languages">Yukaghir languages</a> spoken across Russia</span>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:97px;max-width:97px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:74px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Fenno-Ugrian_languages.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Fenno-Ugrian_languages.png/95px-Fenno-Ugrian_languages.png" decoding="async" width="95" height="75" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Fenno-Ugrian_languages.png/143px-Fenno-Ugrian_languages.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Fenno-Ugrian_languages.png/190px-Fenno-Ugrian_languages.png 2x" data-file-width="1025" data-file-height="808"></a>
