           <span style="font-family:sans-serif;font-size:100%;color:black;background-color:transparent;;"><a href="/wiki/North_Caucasian_languages" title="North Caucasian languages">Languages spoken</a> in the <a href="/wiki/North_Caucasus" title="North Caucasus">North Caucasus</a></span>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Russia's <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> is <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>. However, Russia's 193 minority ethnic groups speak over 100 languages.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-246">[240]</a></sup> According to the 2002 Census, 142.6&nbsp;million people speak Russian, followed by <a href="/wiki/Tatar_language" title="Tatar language">Tatar</a> with 5.3&nbsp;million, and <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_language" title="Ukrainian language">Ukrainian</a> with 1.8&nbsp;million speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[241]</a></sup> The constitution gives the individual republics of the country the right to <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Russia#Official_languages" title="Languages of Russia">establish their own state languages</a> in addition to Russian.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[242]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Russian is the most spoken native language in Europe, the most geographically widespread language of Eurasia, as well as the most widely spoken <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">Slavic language</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[243]</a></sup> It belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-European language">Indo-European language</a> family, is one of the living members of the <a href="/wiki/East_Slavic_languages" title="East Slavic languages">East Slavic languages</a>, and is among the larger <a href="/wiki/Balto-Slavic_languages" title="Balto-Slavic languages">Balto-Slavic languages</a>. It is the second-most used language on the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a> after <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[244]</a></sup> one of two official languages aboard the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[245]</a></sup> and is one of the six <a href="/wiki/Official_languages_of_the_United_Nations" title="Official languages of the United Nations">official languages of the United Nations</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[246]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Russia" title="Religion in Russia">Religion in Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Saint_Basil%27s_Cathedral_in_Moscow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Saint_Basil%27s_Cathedral_in_Moscow.jpg/220px-Saint_Basil%27s_Cathedral_in_Moscow.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="244" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Saint_Basil%27s_Cathedral_in_Moscow.jpg/330px-Saint_Basil%27s_Cathedral_in_Moscow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Saint_Basil%27s_Cathedral_in_Moscow.jpg/440px-Saint_Basil%27s_Cathedral_in_Moscow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="2218"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Saint_Basil%27s_Cathedral_in_Moscow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Saint_Basil%27s_Cathedral" title="Saint Basil's Cathedral">Saint Basil's Cathedral</a> in Moscow; the most popular icon of Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[247]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Russia is a <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a> by constitution, and its largest religion is <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Russia" title="Christianity in Russia">Christianity</a>. It has the world's <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy_by_country" title="Eastern Orthodoxy by country">largest Orthodox population</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[248]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[249]</a></sup> As of a different sociological surveys on religious adherence; between 41% to over 80% of the total population of Russia adhere to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ArenaAtlas2012_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArenaAtlas2012-256">[250]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ogonek_257-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ogonek-257">[251]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[252]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, a survey made by the <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> showed that 73% of Russians declared themselves <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a>âincluding 71% <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Orthodox">Orthodox</a>, 1% <a href="/wiki/Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic">Catholic</a>, and 2% Other Christians, while 15% were <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">unaffiliated</a>, 10% were <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a>, and 1% were from other religions.<sup id="cite_ref-Pew2017_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew2017-5">[4]</a></sup> According to various reports, the proportion of <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">Atheists</a> in Russia is between 16% and 48% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[253]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Russia" title="Islam in Russia">Islam</a> is the second-largest religion in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">[254]</a></sup> It is the traditional and predominant religion amongst the <a href="/wiki/Peoples_of_the_Caucasus" title="Peoples of the Caucasus">peoples of the North Caucasus</a>, and amongst some <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic peoples</a> scattered along the <a href="/wiki/Idel-Ural" title="Idel-Ural">Volga-Ural</a> region. <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Russia" title="Buddhism in Russia">Buddhists</a> are home to a sizeable population in four republics of Russia: <a href="/wiki/Buryatia" title="Buryatia">Buryatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuva" title="Tuva">Tuva</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zabaykalsky_Krai" title="Zabaykalsky Krai">Zabaykalsky Krai</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kalmykia" title="Kalmykia">Kalmykia</a>; the only region in Europe where Buddhism is the most practised religion.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">[255]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> has been a minority faith in Russia, as the country is home to a <a href="/wiki/History_of_Jews_in_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Jews in Russia">historical Jewish population</a>, which is <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Europe" title="History of the Jews in Europe">among the largest in Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[256]</a></sup> In the recent years, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Russia" title="Hinduism in Russia">Hinduism</a> has also seen an increase in followers in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[257]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Russia" title="Education in Russia">Education in Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%93%D0%A3,_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/%D0%9C%D0%93%D0%A3%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0.jpg/220px-%D0%9C%D0%93%D0%A3%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/%D0%9C%D0%93%D0%A3%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0.jpg/330px-%D0%9C%D0%93%D0%A3%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/%D0%9C%D0%93%D0%A3%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0.jpg/440px-%D0%9C%D0%93%D0%A3%2C_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3946" data-file-height="2610"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9C%D0%93%D0%A3,_%D0%B2%D0%B8%D0%B4_%D1%81_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B4%D1%83%D1%85%D0%B0.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Moscow_State_University" title="Moscow State University">Moscow State University</a>, the most prestigious educational institution in Russia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Russia has the highest college-level or higher graduates in terms of percentage of population in the world, at 54%.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[258]</a></sup> It has a <a href="/wiki/Free_education" title="Free education">free education</a> system, which is guaranteed for all citizens by the constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[259]</a></sup> Since 1990, the 11-year school education has been introduced. Education in state-owned secondary schools is free. University-level education is free, with exceptions. A substantial share of students are enrolled for full pay (many state institutions started to open commercial positions in the last years).<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[260]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The oldest and largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_institutions_of_higher_education_in_Russia" title="List of institutions of higher education in Russia">universities</a> in Russia are <a href="/wiki/Moscow_State_University" title="Moscow State University">Moscow State University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg_State_University" title="Saint Petersburg State University">Saint Petersburg State University</a>. In the 2000s, in order to create higher education and research institutions of comparable scale in Russian regions, the government launched a program of establishing federal universities, mostly by merging existing large regional universities and research institutes and providing them with special funding. These new institutions include the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Federal_University" title="Southern Federal University">Southern Federal University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siberian_Federal_University" title="Siberian Federal University">Siberian Federal University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazan_Volga_Federal_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Kazan Volga Federal University">Kazan Volga Federal University</a>, <a href="/wiki/North-Eastern_Federal_University" title="North-Eastern Federal University">North-Eastern Federal University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Far_Eastern_Federal_University" title="Far Eastern Federal University">Far Eastern Federal University</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Russia" title="Healthcare in Russia">Healthcare in Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The constitution of Russia guarantees free, <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a> for all Russian citizens,<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[261]</a></sup> through a compulsory state health insurance program.<sup id="cite_ref-ExpaticaHealth_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ExpaticaHealth-268">[262]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Health_(Russia)" title="Ministry of Health (Russia)">Ministry of Health of the Russian Federation</a> oversees the Russian public healthcare system, and the sector employs more than two million people.<sup id="cite_ref-ExpaticaHealth_268-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ExpaticaHealth-268">[262]</a></sup> Federal regions also have their own departments of health that oversee local administration.<sup id="cite_ref-ExpaticaHealth_268-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ExpaticaHealth-268">[262]</a></sup> Russia has the highest number of physicians, hospitals, and health care workers in the world on a per capita basis.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[263]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, Russia spent 5.32% of its GDP on healthcare in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[264]</a></sup> It has one of the world's most female-biased <a href="/wiki/Human_sex_ratio" title="Human sex ratio">sex ratios</a>, with 0.859 males to every female.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_131-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-131">[127]</a></sup> In 2019, the overall <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">life expectancy in Russia</a> at birth is 73.2 years (68.2 years for males and 78.0 years for females),<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">[265]</a></sup> and it had a very low <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality rate</a> (5 per 1,000 <a href="/wiki/Live_birth_(human)" title="Live birth (human)">live births</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[266]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">Obesity</a> is a major health issue in Russia. In 2016, 61.1% of Russian adults were overweight or obese, while 23.1% were obese.<sup id="cite_ref-RusObese_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RusObese-273">[267]</a></sup> In 2017, roughly 16% of Russia's deaths were attributed to obesity, while per 100,000 Russians, 123 died due to being obese.<sup id="cite_ref-RusObese_273-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RusObese-273">[267]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Russian_culture" title="Russian culture">Russian culture</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art_and_architecture">Art and architecture</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Russian_artists" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian artists">Russian artists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_architecture" title="Russian architecture">Russian architecture</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Russian_architects" title="List of Russian architects">List of Russian architects</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:344px;max-width:344px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:123px;max-width:123px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Angelsatmamre-trinity-rublev-1410.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Angelsatmamre-trinity-rublev-1410.jpg/121px-Angelsatmamre-trinity-rublev-1410.jpg" decoding="async" width="121" height="151" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Angelsatmamre-trinity-rublev-1410.jpg/182px-Angelsatmamre-trinity-rublev-1410.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Angelsatmamre-trinity-rublev-1410.jpg/242px-Angelsatmamre-trinity-rublev-1410.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="1619"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Rublev" title="Andrei Rublev">Andrei Rublev</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Trinity_(Andrei_Rublev)" title="Trinity (Andrei Rublev)">Trinity</a></i> (1425)
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:217px;max-width:217px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Karl_Brullov_-_The_Last_Day_of_Pompeii_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Karl_Brullov_-_The_Last_Day_of_Pompeii_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/215px-Karl_Brullov_-_The_Last_Day_of_Pompeii_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" decoding="async" width="215" height="151" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Karl_Brullov_-_The_Last_Day_of_Pompeii_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/323px-Karl_Brullov_-_The_Last_Day_of_Pompeii_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Karl_Brullov_-_The_Last_Day_of_Pompeii_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/430px-Karl_Brullov_-_The_Last_Day_of_Pompeii_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="30000" data-file-height="21059"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Karl_Bryullov" title="Karl Bryullov">Karl Bryullov</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Day_of_Pompeii" title="The Last Day of Pompeii">The Last Day of Pompeii</a></i> (1833)
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Early Russian painting is represented in <a href="/wiki/Russian_icons" title="Russian icons">icons</a> and vibrant <a href="/wiki/Fresco" title="Fresco">frescos</a>. As Moscow rose to power, <a href="/wiki/Theophanes_the_Greek" title="Theophanes the Greek">Theophanes the Greek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dionisius" title="Dionisius">Dionisius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Rublev" title="Andrei Rublev">Andrei Rublev</a> became vital names in Russian art. The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Arts" title="Russian Academy of Arts">Russian Academy of Arts</a> was created in 1757. In the 18th century, academicians <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Argunov" title="Ivan Argunov">Ivan Argunov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Levitzky" title="Dmitry Levitzky">Dmitry Levitzky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Borovikovsky" title="Vladimir Borovikovsky">Vladimir Borovikovsky</a> became influential. The early 19th century saw many prominent paintings by <a href="/wiki/Karl_Briullov" class="mw-redirect" title="Karl Briullov">Karl Briullov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Andreyevich_Ivanov" title="Alexander Andreyevich Ivanov">Alexander Ivanov</a>. In the mid-19th century, the group of mostly <a href="/wiki/Realism_(arts)" title="Realism (arts)">realists</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Peredvizhniki" title="Peredvizhniki">Peredvizhniki</a></i> broke with the Academy. Leading Russian realists include <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Shishkin" title="Ivan Shishkin">Ivan Shishkin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arkhip_Kuindzhi" title="Arkhip Kuindzhi">Arkhip Kuindzhi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Kramskoi" title="Ivan Kramskoi">Ivan Kramskoi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vasily_Polenov" title="Vasily Polenov">Vasily Polenov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Levitan" title="Isaac Levitan">Isaac Levitan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vasily_Surikov" title="Vasily Surikov">Vasily Surikov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Vasnetsov" title="Viktor Vasnetsov">Viktor Vasnetsov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilya_Repin" title="Ilya Repin">Ilya Repin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boris_Kustodiev" title="Boris Kustodiev">Boris Kustodiev</a>. The turn of the 20th century saw the rise of <a href="/wiki/Symbolism_(arts)" title="Symbolism (arts)">symbolism</a>; represented by <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Vrubel" title="Mikhail Vrubel">Mikhail Vrubel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuzma_Petrov-Vodkin" title="Kuzma Petrov-Vodkin">Kuzma Petrov-Vodkin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Roerich" title="Nicholas Roerich">Nicholas Roerich</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Russian_avant-garde" title="Russian avant-garde">Russian avant-garde</a> flourished from approximately 1890 to 1930; notable artists from this era were <a href="/wiki/El_Lissitzky" title="El Lissitzky">El Lissitzky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazimir_Malevich" title="Kazimir Malevich">Kazimir Malevich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wassily_Kandinsky" title="Wassily Kandinsky">Wassily Kandinsky</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marc_Chagall" title="Marc Chagall">Marc Chagall</a>. Some influential Soviet sculptures were <a href="/wiki/Vera_Mukhina" title="Vera Mukhina">Vera Mukhina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yevgeny_Vuchetich" title="Yevgeny Vuchetich">Yevgeny Vuchetich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Neizvestny" title="Ernst Neizvestny">Ernst Neizvestny</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Saint_Isaac%27s_Cathedral_in_SPB.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Saint_Isaac%27s_Cathedral_in_SPB.jpeg/220px-Saint_Isaac%27s_Cathedral_in_SPB.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Saint_Isaac%27s_Cathedral_in_SPB.jpeg/330px-Saint_Isaac%27s_Cathedral_in_SPB.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Saint_Isaac%27s_Cathedral_in_SPB.jpeg/440px-Saint_Isaac%27s_Cathedral_in_SPB.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="3600" data-file-height="2384"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Saint_Isaac%27s_Cathedral_in_SPB.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Saint_Isaac%27s_Cathedral" title="Saint Isaac's Cathedral">Saint Isaac's Cathedral</a>, an architectural landmark of Saint Petersburg.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Beginning with the woodcraft buildings of ancient <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a>; since the <a href="/wiki/Christianization_of_Kievan_Rus%27" title="Christianization of Kievan Rus'">Christianization of Kievan Rus'</a>, for several centuries Russian architecture was influenced predominantly by <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_architecture" title="Byzantine architecture">Byzantine architecture</a>. <a href="/wiki/Aristotle_Fioravanti" class="mw-redirect" title="Aristotle Fioravanti">Aristotle Fioravanti</a> and other Italian architects brought <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> trends into Russia. The 16th century saw the development of the unique <a href="/wiki/Tent-like_church" class="mw-redirect" title="Tent-like church">tent-like churches</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Onion_dome" title="Onion dome">onion dome</a> design. In the 17th century, the "fiery style" of ornamentation flourished in Moscow and <a href="/wiki/Yaroslavl" title="Yaroslavl">Yaroslavl</a>, gradually paving the way for the <a href="/wiki/Naryshkin_baroque" class="mw-redirect" title="Naryshkin baroque">Naryshkin baroque</a> of the 1690s. After the <a href="/wiki/Reforms_of_Peter_I_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Reforms of Peter I of Russia">reforms of Peter the Great</a>; the country's architecture became influenced by Western Europe. The 18th-century taste for <a href="/wiki/Rococo" title="Rococo">Rococo</a> architecture led to the splendid works of <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeo_Rastrelli" class="mw-redirect" title="Bartolomeo Rastrelli">Bartolomeo Rastrelli</a> and his followers. During the reign of <a href="/wiki/Catherine_the_Great" title="Catherine the Great">Catherine the Great</a> and her grandson <a href="/wiki/Alexander_I_of_Russia" title="Alexander I of Russia">Alexander I</a>, the city of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a> was transformed into an outdoor museum of <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">Neoclassical architecture</a>. The second half of the 19th century was dominated by the Byzantine and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revival" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Revival">Russian Revival</a> style. Prevalent styles of the 20th century were the <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a> (<a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Shekhtel" class="mw-redirect" title="Fyodor Shekhtel">Fyodor Shekhtel</a>), <a href="/wiki/Constructivism_(art)" title="Constructivism (art)">Constructivism</a> (<a href="/wiki/Moisei_Ginzburg" title="Moisei Ginzburg">Moisei Ginzburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victor_Vesnin" class="mw-redirect" title="Victor Vesnin">Victor Vesnin</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Stalinist_architecture" title="Stalinist architecture">Socialist Classicism</a> (<a href="/wiki/Boris_Iofan" title="Boris Iofan">Boris Iofan</a>). </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Russia" title="Music of Russia">Music of Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Portr%C3%A4t_des_Komponisten_Pjotr_I._Tschaikowski_(1840-1893).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Portr%C3%A4t_des_Komponisten_Pjotr_I._Tschaikowski_%281840-1893%29.jpg/170px-Portr%C3%A4t_des_Komponisten_Pjotr_I._Tschaikowski_%281840-1893%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Portr%C3%A4t_des_Komponisten_Pjotr_I._Tschaikowski_%281840-1893%29.jpg/255px-Portr%C3%A4t_des_Komponisten_Pjotr_I._Tschaikowski_%281840-1893%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Portr%C3%A4t_des_Komponisten_Pjotr_I._Tschaikowski_%281840-1893%29.jpg/340px-Portr%C3%A4t_des_Komponisten_Pjotr_I._Tschaikowski_%281840-1893%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="883" data-file-height="1134"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Portr%C3%A4t_des_Komponisten_Pjotr_I._Tschaikowski_(1840-1893).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Ilyich_Tchaikovsky" title="Pyotr Ilyich Tchaikovsky">Pyotr Ilyich Tchaikovsky</a> (1840â1893), composer
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Music in 19th-century Russia was defined by the tension between classical composer <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Glinka" title="Mikhail Glinka">Mikhail Glinka</a> along with other members of <a href="/wiki/The_Mighty_Handful" class="mw-redirect" title="The Mighty Handful">The Mighty Handful</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Musical_Society" title="Russian Musical Society">Russian Musical Society</a> led by composers <a href="/wiki/Anton_Rubinstein" title="Anton Rubinstein">Anton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Rubinstein" class="mw-redirect" title="Nikolay Rubinstein">Nikolay Rubinstein</a>. The later tradition of <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Ilyich_Tchaikovsky" title="Pyotr Ilyich Tchaikovsky">Pyotr Ilyich Tchaikovsky</a>, one of the greatest composers of the <a href="/wiki/Romantic_music" title="Romantic music">Romantic era</a>, was continued into the 20th century by <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Rachmaninoff" title="Sergei Rachmaninoff">Sergei Rachmaninoff</a>, one of the last great champions of the Romantic style of European classical music.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[268]</a></sup> World-renowned composers of the 20th century include <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Scriabin" title="Alexander Scriabin">Alexander Scriabin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Igor_Stravinsky" title="Igor Stravinsky">Igor Stravinsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Prokofiev" title="Sergei Prokofiev">Sergei Prokofiev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dmitri_Shostakovich" title="Dmitri Shostakovich">Dmitri Shostakovich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgy_Sviridov" title="Georgy Sviridov">Georgy Sviridov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Schnittke" title="Alfred Schnittke">Alfred Schnittke</a>. </p>
      <p>Russian conservatories have turned out generations of famous soloists. Among the best known are violinists <a href="/wiki/Jascha_Heifetz" title="Jascha Heifetz">Jascha Heifetz</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Oistrakh" title="David Oistrakh">David Oistrakh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Kogan" title="Leonid Kogan">Leonid Kogan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gidon_Kremer" title="Gidon Kremer">Gidon Kremer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maxim_Vengerov" title="Maxim Vengerov">Maxim Vengerov</a>; cellists <a href="/wiki/Mstislav_Rostropovich" title="Mstislav Rostropovich">Mstislav Rostropovich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natalia_Gutman" title="Natalia Gutman">Natalia Gutman</a>; pianists <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Horowitz" title="Vladimir Horowitz">Vladimir Horowitz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sviatoslav_Richter" title="Sviatoslav Richter">Sviatoslav Richter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emil_Gilels" title="Emil Gilels">Emil Gilels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Sofronitsky" title="Vladimir Sofronitsky">Vladimir Sofronitsky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Evgeny_Kissin" title="Evgeny Kissin">Evgeny Kissin</a>; and vocalists <a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Shalyapin" class="mw-redirect" title="Fyodor Shalyapin">Fyodor Shalyapin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Reizen" title="Mark Reizen">Mark Reizen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elena_Obraztsova" title="Elena Obraztsova">Elena Obraztsova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamara_Sinyavskaya" title="Tamara Sinyavskaya">Tamara Sinyavskaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nina_Dorliak" title="Nina Dorliak">Nina Dorliak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galina_Vishnevskaya" title="Galina Vishnevskaya">Galina Vishnevskaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anna_Netrebko" title="Anna Netrebko">Anna Netrebko</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Hvorostovsky" class="mw-redirect" title="Dmitry Hvorostovsky">Dmitry Hvorostovsky</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[269]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Modern <a href="/wiki/Russian_rock" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian rock">Russian rock</a> music takes its roots both in the Western <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a>, and in traditions of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_bards" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian bards">Russian bards</a> of the Soviet era, such as <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Vysotsky" title="Vladimir Vysotsky">Vladimir Vysotsky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulat_Okudzhava" title="Bulat Okudzhava">Bulat Okudzhava</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[270]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Russian_pop" title="Russian pop">Russian pop</a> music developed from what was known in the Soviet times as <i>estrada</i> into a full-fledged industry. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature_and_philosophy">Literature and philosophy</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Russian_literature" title="Russian literature">Russian literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_philosophy" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian philosophy">Russian philosophy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_poets" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian poets">Russian poets</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_playwrights" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian playwrights">Russian playwrights</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_novelists" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian novelists">Russian novelists</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russian_science_fiction_and_fantasy" title="Russian science fiction and fantasy">Russian science fiction and fantasy</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ilya_Efimovich_Repin_(1844-1930)_-_Portrait_of_Leo_Tolstoy_(1887).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Ilya_Efimovich_Repin_%281844-1930%29_-_Portrait_of_Leo_Tolstoy_%281887%29.jpg/170px-Ilya_Efimovich_Repin_%281844-1930%29_-_Portrait_of_Leo_Tolstoy_%281887%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Ilya_Efimovich_Repin_%281844-1930%29_-_Portrait_of_Leo_Tolstoy_%281887%29.jpg/255px-Ilya_Efimovich_Repin_%281844-1930%29_-_Portrait_of_Leo_Tolstoy_%281887%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Ilya_Efimovich_Repin_%281844-1930%29_-_Portrait_of_Leo_Tolstoy_%281887%29.jpg/340px-Ilya_Efimovich_Repin_%281844-1930%29_-_Portrait_of_Leo_Tolstoy_%281887%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1508" data-file-height="2048"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ilya_Efimovich_Repin_(1844-1930)_-_Portrait_of_Leo_Tolstoy_(1887).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Leo_Tolstoy" title="Leo Tolstoy">Leo Tolstoy</a> is regarded as one of the greatest authors of all time.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Russian_literature" title="Russian literature">Russian literature</a> is considered to be among the most influential and developed in the world. It can be traced back to the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, when epics and chronicles in <a href="/wiki/Old_East_Slavic" title="Old East Slavic">Old East Slavic</a> were composed. In the 18th century, by the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Age of Enlightenment</a>, the works of <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lomonosov" title="Mikhail Lomonosov">Mikhail Lomonosov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denis_Fonvizin" title="Denis Fonvizin">Denis Fonvizin</a> boosted Russian literature. The early 19th century began with <a href="/wiki/Vasily_Zhukovsky" title="Vasily Zhukovsky">Vasily Zhukovsky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Pushkin" title="Alexander Pushkin">Alexander Pushkin</a>; who is considered by many to be the greatest Russian poet.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">[271]</a></sup> It continued with the poetry of <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Lermontov" title="Mikhail Lermontov">Mikhail Lermontov</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Nekrasov" title="Nikolay Nekrasov">Nikolay Nekrasov</a>, dramas of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Ostrovsky" title="Alexander Ostrovsky">Alexander Ostrovsky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anton_Chekhov" title="Anton Chekhov">Anton Chekhov</a>, and the prose of <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Gogol" title="Nikolai Gogol">Nikolai Gogol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Turgenev" title="Ivan Turgenev">Ivan Turgenev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Saltykov-Shchedrin" title="Mikhail Saltykov-Shchedrin">Mikhail Saltykov-Shchedrin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Goncharov" title="Ivan Goncharov">Ivan Goncharov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aleksey_Pisemsky" title="Aleksey Pisemsky">Aleksey Pisemsky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Leskov" title="Nikolai Leskov">Nikolai Leskov</a>. <a href="/wiki/Leo_Tolstoy" title="Leo Tolstoy">Leo Tolstoy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fyodor_Dostoevsky" title="Fyodor Dostoevsky">Fyodor Dostoevsky</a> have been described by as the greatest novelists of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[272]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[273]</a></sup> The next several decades had leading authors such as <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Balmont" title="Konstantin Balmont">Konstantin Balmont</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valery_Bryusov" title="Valery Bryusov">Valery Bryusov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vyacheslav_Ivanov_(poet)" title="Vyacheslav Ivanov (poet)">Vyacheslav Ivanov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Blok" title="Alexander Blok">Alexander Blok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Gumilyov" title="Nikolay Gumilyov">Nikolay Gumilyov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Merezhkovsky" title="Dmitry Merezhkovsky">Dmitry Merezhkovsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anna_Akhmatova" title="Anna Akhmatova">Anna Akhmatova</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Boris_Pasternak" title="Boris Pasternak">Boris Pasternak</a>; and novelists <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Andreyev" title="Leonid Andreyev">Leonid Andreyev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Bunin" title="Ivan Bunin">Ivan Bunin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Maxim_Gorky" title="Maxim Gorky">Maxim Gorky</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Russian_philosophy" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian philosophy">Russian philosophy</a> blossomed in the 19th century; with the works of <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Danilevsky" title="Nikolay Danilevsky">Nikolay Danilevsky</a> and <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Leontiev" title="Konstantin Leontiev">Konstantin Leontiev</a>. Notable philosophers of the late 19th and early 20th centuries include <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Solovyov_(philosopher)" title="Vladimir Solovyov (philosopher)">Vladimir Solovyov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Bulgakov" title="Sergei Bulgakov">Sergei Bulgakov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Florensky" title="Pavel Florensky">Pavel Florensky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikolai_Berdyaev" title="Nikolai Berdyaev">Nikolai Berdyaev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lossky" title="Vladimir Lossky">Vladimir Lossky</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Vernadsky" title="Vladimir Vernadsky">Vladimir Vernadsky</a>. </p>
      <p>Following the 1917 revolution, and the ensuing civil war, many prominent writers and philosophers left the country; while a new generation of authors joined together in an effort to create a distinctive <a href="/wiki/Working-class_culture" title="Working-class culture">working-class culture</a> appropriate for the new Soviet state. Leading authors of the Soviet era include novelists <a href="/wiki/Yevgeny_Zamyatin" title="Yevgeny Zamyatin">Yevgeny Zamiatin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Babel" title="Isaac Babel">Isaac Babel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Mayakovsky" title="Vladimir Mayakovsky">Vladimir Mayakovsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilf_and_Petrov" title="Ilf and Petrov">Ilf and Petrov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yury_Olesha" title="Yury Olesha">Yury Olesha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Bulgakov" title="Mikhail Bulgakov">Mikhail Bulgakov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Sholokhov" title="Mikhail Sholokhov">Mikhail Sholokhov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Solzhenitsyn" title="Aleksandr Solzhenitsyn">Aleksandr Solzhenitsyn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yevgeny_Yevtushenko" title="Yevgeny Yevtushenko">Yevgeny Yevtushenko</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Voznesensky" title="Andrei Voznesensky">Andrei Voznesensky</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Russian_cuisine" title="Russian cuisine">Russian cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mint_bread_kvas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Mint_bread_kvas.jpg/220px-Mint_bread_kvas.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Mint_bread_kvas.jpg/330px-Mint_bread_kvas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Mint_bread_kvas.jpg/440px-Mint_bread_kvas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2628" data-file-height="1971"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mint_bread_kvas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Kvass" title="Kvass">Kvass</a> is an ancient and traditional Russian beverage.<sup id="cite_ref-Kvass_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kvass-280">[274]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Russian_cuisine" title="Russian cuisine">Russian cuisine</a> has been formed by climate, cultural and religious traditions, and the vast geography of the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[275]</a></sup> It shares many similarities with cuisines of its neighbouring countries, and widely uses vegetables, fish, flour, cereals, <a href="/wiki/Bread_in_Europe#Finland_and_Russia" title="Bread in Europe">bread</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-bread_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bread-282">[276]</a></sup> and berries.<sup id="cite_ref-Trafalgar_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trafalgar-283">[277]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Crops of <a href="/wiki/Rye" title="Rye">rye</a>, wheat, <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">barley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a> provide the ingredients for various breads, <a href="/wiki/Pancake" title="Pancake">pancakes</a> and cereals, as well as for many drinks. <a href="/wiki/Black_bread" class="mw-redirect" title="Black bread">Black bread</a> is very popular in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-bread_282-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bread-282">[276]</a></sup> Flavourful soups and stews include <a href="/wiki/Shchi" title="Shchi">shchi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borsch" class="mw-redirect" title="Borsch">borsch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukha" title="Ukha">ukha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solyanka" title="Solyanka">solyanka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Okroshka" title="Okroshka">okroshka</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Trafalgar_283-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trafalgar-283">[277]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Smetana_(dairy_product)" title="Smetana (dairy product)">Smetana</a> (a heavy <a href="/wiki/Sour_cream" title="Sour cream">sour cream</a>) is often added to soups and salads.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[278]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pirozhki" title="Pirozhki">Pirozhki</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blini" title="Blini">blini</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syrniki" title="Syrniki">syrniki</a> are native types of pancakes.<sup id="cite_ref-Trafalgar_283-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trafalgar-283">[277]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Beef_Stroganoff" title="Beef Stroganoff">Beef Stroganoff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicken_Kiev" title="Chicken Kiev">Chicken Kiev</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pelmeni" title="Pelmeni">pelmeni</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shashlyk" class="mw-redirect" title="Shashlyk">shashlyk</a> are popular meat dishes.<sup id="cite_ref-Atlas_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Atlas-285">[279]</a></sup> Other meat dishes include stuffed cabbage rolls <i>(<a href="/wiki/Golubtsy" class="mw-redirect" title="Golubtsy">golubtsy</a>)</i> usually filled with meat.<sup id="cite_ref-mrig-golubtsy_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mrig-golubtsy-286">[280]</a></sup> Salads include <a href="/wiki/Olivier_salad" title="Olivier salad">Olivier salad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vinegret" title="Vinegret">vinegret</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dressed_herring" title="Dressed herring">dressed herring</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Atlas_285-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Atlas-285">[279]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Russia's <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_drinks" title="List of national drinks">national non-alcoholic drink</a> is <a href="/wiki/Kvass" title="Kvass">Kvass</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Kvass_280-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kvass-280">[274]</a></sup> and the national alcoholic drink is <a href="/wiki/Vodka" title="Vodka">vodka</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[281]</a></sup> its creation in the nation dates back to the 14th century.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">[282]</a></sup> The country has the world's highest vodka consumption,<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[283]</a></sup> but <a href="/wiki/Beer_in_Russia" title="Beer in Russia">beer</a> is the most popular alcoholic beverage in Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-SCMP_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCMP-290">[284]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Russian_wine" title="Russian wine">Wine</a> has become popular in Russia in the last decade,<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[285]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[286]</a></sup> and the country is becoming one of the world's largest wine producers.<sup id="cite_ref-SCMP_290-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SCMP-290">[284]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[287]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Russia">Media of Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Russia" title="Cinema of Russia">Cinema of Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vintage_Potemkin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Vintage_Potemkin.jpg/170px-Vintage_Potemkin.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Vintage_Potemkin.jpg/255px-Vintage_Potemkin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Vintage_Potemkin.jpg/340px-Vintage_Potemkin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3541" data-file-height="5000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vintage_Potemkin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Poster of <i><a href="/wiki/Battleship_Potemkin" title="Battleship Potemkin">Battleship Potemkin</a></i> (1925) by <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Eisenstein" title="Sergei Eisenstein">Sergei Eisenstein</a>, which was named the <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_considered_the_best" title="List of films considered the best">greatest film of all time</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Expo_58" title="Expo 58">Brussels World's Fair</a> in 1958
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The largest internationally operating news agencies in Russia are <a href="/wiki/TASS" title="TASS">TASS</a>, <a href="/wiki/RIA_Novosti" title="RIA Novosti">RIA Novosti</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Interfax" title="Interfax">Interfax</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[288]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Russia" title="Television in Russia">Television</a> is the most popular media in Russia, with 74% of the population watching national television channels routinely, and 59% routinely watching regional channels.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[289]</a></sup> There are three main nationwide radio stations in Russia: <a href="/wiki/Radio_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio Russia">Radio Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radio_Mayak" title="Radio Mayak">Radio Mayak</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Radio_Yunost" title="Radio Yunost">Radio Yunost</a>. Russia has the <a href="/wiki/Video_games_in_Russia" title="Video games in Russia">largest video gaming market</a> in Europe, with over 65 million players nationwide.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[290]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Russian and later <a href="/wiki/Soviet_cinema" class="mw-redirect" title="Soviet cinema">Soviet cinema</a> was a hotbed of invention, resulting in world-renowned films such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Battleship_Potemkin" class="mw-redirect" title="The Battleship Potemkin">The Battleship Potemkin</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[291]</a></sup> Soviet-era filmmakers, most notably <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Eisenstein" title="Sergei Eisenstein">Sergei Eisenstein</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Tarkovsky" title="Andrei Tarkovsky">Andrei Tarkovsky</a>, would become some of the world's most innovative and influential directors. <a href="/wiki/Lev_Kuleshov" title="Lev Kuleshov">Lev Kuleshov</a> developed the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_montage_theory" title="Soviet montage theory">Soviet montage theory</a>, and was one of the founders of the <a href="/wiki/Gerasimov_Institute_of_Cinematography" title="Gerasimov Institute of Cinematography">Moscow Film School</a>, the world's first <a href="/wiki/Film_school" title="Film school">film school</a>. <a href="/wiki/Dziga_Vertov" title="Dziga Vertov">Dziga Vertov</a>'s "film-eye" theory had a huge impact on the development of documentary filmmaking and cinema realism. Many Soviet socialist realism films were artistically successful, including <i><a href="/wiki/Chapaev_(film)" title="Chapaev (film)">Chapaev</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cranes_Are_Flying" title="The Cranes Are Flying">The Cranes Are Flying</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Ballad_of_a_Soldier" title="Ballad of a Soldier">Ballad of a Soldier</a></i>. </p>
      <p>The 1960s and 1970s saw a greater variety of artistic styles in Soviet cinema. <a href="/wiki/Eldar_Ryazanov" title="Eldar Ryazanov">Eldar Ryazanov</a>'s and <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Gaidai" title="Leonid Gaidai">Leonid Gaidai</a>'s comedies of that time were immensely popular, with many of the catchphrases still in use today. In 1961â68 <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Bondarchuk" class="mw-redirect" title="Sergey Bondarchuk">Sergey Bondarchuk</a> directed an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Oscar</a>-winning <a href="/wiki/War_and_Peace_(film_series)" title="War and Peace (film series)">film adaptation</a> of Leo Tolstoy's epic <i><a href="/wiki/War_and_Peace" title="War and Peace">War and Peace</a></i>, which was <a href="/wiki/The_most_expensive_film" class="mw-redirect" title="The most expensive film">the most expensive film</a> made in the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[292]</a></sup> In 1969, <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Motyl" title="Vladimir Motyl">Vladimir Motyl</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/White_Sun_of_the_Desert" title="White Sun of the Desert">White Sun of the Desert</a></i> was released, a very popular film in a genre of <a href="/wiki/Ostern" title="Ostern">ostern</a>; the film is traditionally watched by <a href="/wiki/Cosmonauts" class="mw-redirect" title="Cosmonauts">cosmonauts</a> before any trip into space.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[293]</a></sup> In 2002, <i><a href="/wiki/Russian_Ark" title="Russian Ark">Russian Ark</a></i> was the first feature film ever to be shot in a single take.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[294]</a></sup> Today, the Russian cinema industry continues to expand.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[295]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Russia" title="Sport in Russia">Sport in Russia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Maria_Sharapova_(18405201199).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Maria_Sharapova_%2818405201199%29.jpg/220px-Maria_Sharapova_%2818405201199%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Maria_Sharapova_%2818405201199%29.jpg/330px-Maria_Sharapova_%2818405201199%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Maria_Sharapova_%2818405201199%29.jpg/440px-Maria_Sharapova_%2818405201199%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4483" data-file-height="3287"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Maria_Sharapova_(18405201199).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Maria_Sharapova" title="Maria Sharapova">Maria Sharapova</a>, former <a href="/wiki/List_of_WTA_number_1_ranked_tennis_players" title="List of WTA number 1 ranked tennis players">world No. 1</a> tennis player; and the world's highest-paid female athlete for 11 consecutive years.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[296]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is one of the most popular sports in Russia. The Soviet national team became the first European Champions by winning <a href="/wiki/Euro_1960" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro 1960">Euro 1960</a>; and reached the finals of <a href="/wiki/Euro_1988" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro 1988">Euro 1988</a>. In 1956 and 1988, the Soviet Union won gold at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_Summer_Olympics#Men's_results" title="Football at the Summer Olympics">Olympic football tournament</a>. Russian clubs <a href="/wiki/PFC_CSKA_Moscow" title="PFC CSKA Moscow">CSKA Moscow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zenit_Saint_Petersburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Zenit Saint Petersburg">Zenit Saint Petersburg</a> won the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a> in 2005 and 2008. The <a href="/wiki/Russian_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian national football team">Russian national football team</a> reached the semi-finals of <a href="/wiki/Euro_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro 2008">Euro 2008</a>. Russia was the host nation for the <a href="/wiki/2017_FIFA_Confederations_Cup" title="2017 FIFA Confederations Cup">2017 FIFA Confederations Cup</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">Ice hockey</a> is very popular in Russia. The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="Soviet Union men's national ice hockey team">Soviet national ice hockey team</a> dominated the sport internationally throughout its existence, winning gold at seven of the nine <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey_at_the_Olympic_Games" title="Ice hockey at the Olympic Games">Olympics</a> and 19 of the 30 <a href="/wiki/Ice_Hockey_World_Championships" title="Ice Hockey World Championships">World Championships</a> they contested between 1954 and 1991. The <a href="/wiki/Russia_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="Russia men's national ice hockey team">Russia men's national ice hockey team</a> won the <a href="/wiki/1993_IIHF_World_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="1993 IIHF World Championship">1993</a>, <a href="/wiki/2008_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2008 IIHF World Championship">2008</a>, <a href="/wiki/2009_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2009 IIHF World Championship">2009</a>, <a href="/wiki/2012_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2012 IIHF World Championship">2012</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2014_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2014 IIHF World Championship">2014 IIHF World Championships</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bandy" title="Bandy">Bandy</a> is another traditionally popular ice sport in the country. The Soviet Union won all the <a href="/wiki/Bandy_World_Championship" title="Bandy World Championship">Bandy World Championships</a> for men between 1957 and 1979,<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[297]</a></sup> and some thereafter too. The <a href="/wiki/Russia_national_bandy_team" title="Russia national bandy team">Russia national bandy team</a> has won the <a href="/wiki/Bandy_World_Championship" title="Bandy World Championship">Bandy World Championship</a> in <a href="/wiki/1999_Bandy_World_Championship" title="1999 Bandy World Championship">1999</a>, <a href="/wiki/2001_Bandy_World_Championship" title="2001 Bandy World Championship">2001</a>, <a href="/wiki/2006_Bandy_World_Championship" title="2006 Bandy World Championship">2006</a>, <a href="/wiki/2007_Bandy_World_Championship" title="2007 Bandy World Championship">2007</a>, <a href="/wiki/2008_Bandy_World_Championship" title="2008 Bandy World Championship">2008</a>, <a href="/wiki/2011_Bandy_World_Championship" title="2011 Bandy World Championship">2011</a>, and has been the reigning world champion since <a href="/wiki/2013_Bandy_World_Championship" title="2013 Bandy World Championship">2013</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Russian_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian national basketball team">Russian national basketball team</a> won the <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket_2007" title="EuroBasket 2007">EuroBasket 2007</a>; and the Russian basketball club <a href="/wiki/PBC_CSKA_Moscow" title="PBC CSKA Moscow">PBC CSKA Moscow</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Euroleague" class="mw-redirect" title="Euroleague">Euroleague</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Euroleague" title="2005â06 Euroleague">2006</a> and <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Euroleague" title="2007â08 Euroleague">2008</a>. <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> is also becoming increasingly popular in Russia. </p>
      <p>Historically, <a href="/wiki/Russia_at_the_Olympics" title="Russia at the Olympics">Russian athletes</a> have been one of the most successful contenders in the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-Parks2016_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parks2016-304">[298]</a></sup> ranking third in an <a href="/wiki/All-time_Olympic_Games_medal_table" title="All-time Olympic Games medal table">all-time Olympic Games medal count</a>. <a href="/wiki/Larisa_Latynina" title="Larisa Latynina">Larisa Latynina</a> holds the record for the most gold Olympic medals won by a woman. Olympic gold medalist <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Popov_(swimmer)" title="Alexander Popov (swimmer)">Alexander Popov</a> is widely considered the greatest sprint swimmer in history.<sup id="cite_ref-GrassoMallon2015_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GrassoMallon2015-305">[299]</a></sup> Russia is the leading nation in <a href="/wiki/Rhythmic_gymnastics" title="Rhythmic gymnastics">rhythmic gymnastics</a>; and Russian <a href="/wiki/Synchronized_swimming" title="Synchronized swimming">synchronized swimming</a> is the best in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[300]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Figure_skating" title="Figure skating">Figure skating</a> is another popular sport in Russia, especially <a href="/wiki/Pair_skating" title="Pair skating">pair skating</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ice_dancing" class="mw-redirect" title="Ice dancing">ice dancing</a>. Russia has produced a number of famous <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a> players. <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">Chess</a> is also a widely popular pastime, with many of the world's top chess players being Russian for decades, the likes of <a href="/wiki/Garry_Kasparov" title="Garry Kasparov">Garry Kasparov</a>. The <a href="/wiki/1980_Summer_Olympic_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="1980 Summer Olympic Games">1980 Summer Olympic Games</a> were held in Moscow, and the <a href="/wiki/2014_Winter_Olympics" title="2014 Winter Olympics">2014 Winter Olympics</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2014_Winter_Paralympics" title="2014 Winter Paralympics">2014 Winter Paralympics</a> were hosted in Sochi. </p>

       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a>, which was <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexed by Russia</a> in 2014, is still <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly_Resolution_68/262" title="United Nations General Assembly Resolution 68/262">internationally recognised</a> as an integral part of <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-Areanote-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Areanote_8-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Excluding <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a>, whose 2014 annexation by Russia is not recognized internationally. Including that territory the total land area of Russia increases to 17,125,191&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (6,612,073&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Russian: <span lang="ru" title="Russian-language text">Ð Ð¾ÑÑÐ¸Ð¹ÑÐºÐ°Ñ Ð¤ÐµÐ´ÐµÑÐ°ÑÐ¸Ñ</span>, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Russian" title="Romanization of Russian">tr.</a></small> <i lang="ru-Latn" title="Russian-language text">Rossiyskaya Federatsiya</i>, <small>IPA:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian" title="Help:IPA/Russian">[rÉËsÊ²ijskÉjÉ fÊ²ÉªdÊ²ÉªËratsÉ¨jÉ]</a></span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-116"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-116">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Including the disputed <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea" title="Republic of Crimea">Republic of Crimea</a>, and the federal city of <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a>.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-155"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-155">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Russia has an additional 850&nbsp;km (530&nbsp;mi) of coastline along the Caspian Sea, which is inland, and therefore landlocked.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-157"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-157">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">These points are: from the <a href="/wiki/Vistula_Spit" title="Vistula Spit">Vistula Spit</a> and the southeasternmost point of the <a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands" title="Kuril Islands">Kuril Islands</a>. The points which are farthest separated in <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">longitude</a> are 6,600&nbsp;km (4,101&nbsp;mi) apart along a geodesic line. These points are: In the west, the same spit, and in the east, the <a href="/wiki/Big_Diomede_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Diomede Island">Big Diomede Island</a>.</span> </li>

        <li id="cite_note-254"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-254">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.pewforum.org/2017/05/10/religious-belief-and-national-belonging-in-central-and-eastern-europe/">"Religious Belief and National Belonging in Central and Eastern Europe"</a>. <i>Pew Research Center's Religion &amp; Public Life Project</i>. 10 May 2017.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Pew+Research+Center%27s+Religion+%26+Public+Life+Project&amp;rft.atitle=Religious+Belief+and+National+Belonging+in+Central+and+Eastern+Europe&amp;rft.date=2017-05-10&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.pewforum.org%2F2017%2F05%2F10%2Freligious-belief-and-national-belonging-in-central-and-eastern-europe%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARussia" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-255"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-255">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite class="citation web cs1"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.pewforum.org/2017/11/08/orthodox-christianity-in-the-21st-century/">"Orthodox Christianity in the 21st Century"</a>. <i>Pew Research Center's Religion &amp; Public Life Project</i>. 10 November 2017.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Pew+Research+Center%27s+Religion+%26+Public+Life+Project&amp;rft.atitle=Orthodox+Christianity+in+the+21st+Century&amp;rft.date=2017-11-10&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.pewforum.org%2F2017%2F11%2F08%2Forthodox-christianity-in-the-21st-century%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ARussia" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-ArenaAtlas2012-256"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-ArenaAtlas2012_256-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">There is no official census of religion in Russia, and estimates are based on surveys only. In August 2012, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://sreda.org/arena">ARENA</a> determined that about 46.8% of Russians are Christians (including Orthodox, Catholic, Protestant, and non-denominational), which is slightly less than an absolute 50%+ majority. However, later that year the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.levada.ru/17-12-2012/v-rossii-74-pravoslavnykh-i-7-musulman">Levada Center</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20121231020830/http://www.levada.ru/17-12-2012/v-rossii-74-pravoslavnykh-i-7-musulman">Archived</a> 31 December 2012 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a> determined that 76% of Russians are Christians, and in June 2013 the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://fom.ru/obshchestvo/10953">Public Opinion Foundation</a> determined that 65% of Russians are Christians. These findings are in line with <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.pewforum.org/2011/12/19/global-christianity-exec/">Pew</a>'s 2010 survey, which determined that 73.3% of Russians are Christians, with <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://wciom.ru/index.php?id=268&amp;uid=13365">VTSIOM</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20200929201730/https://wciom.ru/index.php?id=268&amp;uid=13365%2F">Archived</a> 29 September 2020 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>'s 2010 survey (~77% Christian), and with <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.fgi-tbff.org/sites/default/files/elfinder/FGIImages/Research/fromresearchtopolicy/ipsos_mori_briefing_pack.pdf#page=40">Ipsos MORI</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20130117013643/http://www.fgi-tbff.org/sites/default/files/elfinder/FGIImages/Research/fromresearchtopolicy/ipsos_mori_briefing_pack.pdf">Archived</a> 17 January 2013 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>'s 2011 survey (69%).</span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-Ogonek-257"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Ogonek_257-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.kommersant.ru/doc/1997068">ÐÐµÑÑ â Ð½Ðµ Ð²ÐµÑÑ</a>. "Ogonek", â 34 (5243), 27 August 2012. Retrieved 24 September 2012.</span> </li>

                      </ul>

                   </tr>
                   <tr>
                    <td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2">
                     <div> 
                      <ul>
                       <li><sup>1</sup>Claimed by <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> and considered by most of the international community to be part of Ukraine</li>

                   <li><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Emblem_of_the_Office_of_the_Prosecutor_General_of_Russia.svg" class="image"><img alt="Emblem of the Office of the Prosecutor General of Russia.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Emblem_of_the_Office_of_the_Prosecutor_General_of_Russia.svg/20px-Emblem_of_the_Office_of_the_Prosecutor_General_of_Russia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="21" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Emblem_of_the_Office_of_the_Prosecutor_General_of_Russia.svg/30px-Emblem_of_the_Office_of_the_Prosecutor_General_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Emblem_of_the_Office_of_the_Prosecutor_General_of_Russia.svg/40px-Emblem_of_the_Office_of_the_Prosecutor_General_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="524" data-file-height="558"></a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prosecutor_Generals_of_Russia_and_the_Soviet_Union" title="List of Prosecutor Generals of Russia and the Soviet Union">Prosecutors general</a></span></li>
